Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Principle 9: Ease and Convenience Preferred
Presents the principle preferring the statement that brings ease to people

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the ease principle applies and apply it to resolve conflicting corrected statements.

Core Idea
When two conflicting corrected statements are equal in other tarjih factors, the easier one is preferred — Shariah favours ease.

In the process of issuing fatwas, a mufti often encounters conflicting corrected statements from the school. This principle, the ninth in the series, provides a crucial tiebreaker: when all other tarjih factors are equal, the statement that brings ease and avoids hardship is given precedence. This reflects the overall maqasid of the Shariah to facilitate worship and transactions.

Guided Path
1
Confirm conflicting corrected statements
Ensure both statements are sahih (correct) and mu'tamad (relied upon) within the school, and that they genuinely conflict on the same issue.
2
Assess all other tarjih factors
Check if any other preponderance factor exists, such as stronger textual evidence, majority of companions, or analogical reasoning. The ease principle only applies when these are equal.
3
Identify the easier statement
Consider the practical impact on the people: which ruling involves less difficulty (haraj) and more convenience (taysir)?
4
Apply the principle
The easier statement becomes raajih (preponderant) and is chosen as the mufta bihi.
This principle is not a license to always pick the easy way; it is the last resort after all other factors are equal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نواں اصول بسہولت والا قول راجح ہوگا دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ایک قول میں لوگوں کے لئے سہولت اور آسانی ہو اور دوسرے قول میں لوگوں کے لئے حرج اور تنگی ہو تو شریعت کے مزاج و مذاق کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس میں آسانی ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى : ١٤٦ ، اصول الافتاء و آدابه: ٢٢٦)
Ninth principle: The statement with ease will be preferred. Among two conflicting corrected statements, if one statement contains facility and ease for the people and the other statement contains hardship and difficulty for the people, then, considering the temperament and taste of the Shariah, the statement that contains ease will be given preference.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This final principle applies a general maqasid approach: the Shariah aims to bring ease (taysir) and remove hardship (haraj). When two corrected statements conflict and all other factors are equal, the one that is easier for the people to practice is given preference. This reflects the famous maxim 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir' (hardship begets ease). The mufti must consider the overall spirit and objectives of the Shariah, not just technical legal reasoning. The principle is sourced from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti and Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuh.

Key Terms
مزاج و مذاق شریعت (Mizaj wa mazaq al-shari'ah): The overall temperament and spirit of the Islamic law, which inclines towards ease.
ترجیح (Tarjih): The process of giving preference to one legal opinion over another based on preponderance factors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the easier statement preferred according to the ninth principle?
A) Always, because Shariah always prefers ease
B) When the two conflicting statements are equal in all other aspects of preference
C) Only when the issue is related to worship
D) Only when the issue is related to transactions

Key Takeaway
The ease principle is a tiebreaker for conflicting corrected statements; it gives preference to the easier option when all other tarjih factors are equal.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Seventh Principle: Istihsan over Qiyas
Rule for preferring istihsan over qiyas in conflicting fatwas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of preferring an istihsan-based qawl over a qiyas-based qawl when two corrected opinions conflict, and identify the known exceptions where qiyas is preferred.

Core Idea
Between two conflicting corrected opinions, the one based on istihsan prevails over qiyas because istihsan has greater legal strength.

This lesson covers the seventh principle of tarjih in Rasm al-Mufti. When two corrected opinions conflict, the mufti must prefer the one based on istihsan (juristic preference) over one based on qiyas (analogy). However, this rule is not absolute; there are a few known issues where qiyas is given precedence instead of istihsan. Later scholars have enumerated these exceptions with detailed explanations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting opinions
First, confirm that both opinions are 'corrected' (musahhah) and that they conflict on the same case. The principle only applies to tas-hih, not to every fatwa.
2
Determine the basis of each opinion
Analyze the legal reasoning behind each opinion: which one relies on istihsan and which on qiyas? The basis is often indicated by the author's commentary.
If both are based on the same source, other principles apply.
3
Apply the tarjih rule
Prefer the opinion based on istihsan, because istihsan has greater strength than qiyas in the Hanafi school. This is the default ruling.
4
Check for exceptions
Review whether the case is among the enumerated exceptions where qiyas is preferred. If it is, apply qiyas instead of istihsan.
The number of exceptions varies by scholar; the most detailed count is 26 (per Mufti Salman Mansurpuri).
5
Formulate the fatwa
After determining which basis is preferred, state the fatwa accordingly. If neither basis is clearly stronger, the mufti must fall back on other tarjih principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتواں اصول : استحسان قیاس پر راج ہوگا
دو متعارض تصحیح شد و اقوال میں سے جس قول کی بنیاد استحسان پر ہوگی اس قول کو قیاس والے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، کیوں کہ قیاس کے مقابلہ میں استحسان کے اندر زیادہ قوت ہوتی ہے، پس اسی کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی لیکن چند مسائل ایسے ہیں جہاں استحسان کو چھوڑ کر
قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٤٥) واضح ہو کہ راجح قیاسی مسائل کی تعداد علامہ ناطفی کی الاجناس میں اار بیان کی گئی ہے، جبکہ امام نجم الدین النسفی کے یہاں ایسے مسائل کی تعداد ۲ رہے۔ (اعضا ۱۲۹) نوٹ: حضرت اقدس مفتی سلمان منصور پوری نے انتہائی تحقیق اور تلاش بسیار کے بعد فتوی نویسی کے رہنما اصول (صفحه ۲۳۴۰ تا ۲۵۴ ) میں ان مسائل کی تعداد ۲۶ / بیان کی ہے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کی دل نشیں وضاحت بھی کی ہے۔
Seventh Principle: Istihsan overrides Qiyas. Between two conflicting corrected opinions, whichever opinion is based on istihsan will have preference over the opinion based on qiyas, because istihsan has greater strength compared to qiyas, so it will have preference. But there are a few issues where qiyas will be acted upon leaving istihsan. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 145) It is clear that the number of rajih qiyasi issues has been mentioned by Allamah Natafi in his al-Ajnas, while Imam Najm al-Din al-Nasafi counts such issues as 2. Note: Hadrat Aqdas Mufti Salman Mansurpuri, after extreme research and extensive search, in his Fatawa Navisi ke Rehnuma Usul (pages 2340-254) has stated the number of these issues as 26 and has provided a delightful explanation of each.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This is the seventh principle of preference (tarjih) among conflicting fatwa opinions. The author states that when a ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and another on qiyas (analogy), the istihsan-based ruling is given precedence because it carries greater legal strength. However, this is not absolute; there are exceptions where qiyas is followed instead. The text then notes differing counts of these exceptional cases among scholars: Allamah Natafi and Imam Najm al-Din al-Nasafi give different numbers, and later Mufti Salman Mansurpuri identified 26 such cases with detailed explanation.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that deviates from strict qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling, based on stronger evidence or public interest.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the seventh principle, which type of qawl is given preference between two conflicting corrected opinions?
A) The qawl based on qiyas
B) The qawl based on istihsan
C) The qawl with more textual evidence
D) The qawl preferred by the majority of scholars

Key Takeaway
When two corrected opinions conflict, prefer istihsan over qiyas, but be mindful of the few known exceptions where qiyas is given precedence.

The Eighth Principle: Anfa' lil-Waqf
Rule for preferring the opinion most beneficial to the waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of 'anfa' lil-waqf' to prefer one conflicting opinion over another in waqf-related fatwas.

Core Idea
When two opinions conflict, prefer the one more beneficial to the waqf, its founder, and beneficiaries.

When issuing fatwas on waqf matters, muftis sometimes find two conflicting but equally authenticated rulings. The eighth principle of Rasm al-Mufti provides a clear criterion: choose the opinion that brings greater benefit to the entire waqf arrangement. This ensures the founder's intent is fulfilled and the endowment's utility is maximized.

Guided Path
1
Confirm conflicting opinions are equally sound
Ensure both opinions have been corrected (tashih) and are equally authoritative. The principle applies only when neither can be dismissed outright.
This rule does not apply if one opinion is weak or rejected.
2
Identify the three waqf stakeholders
The waqif (founder), the mawquf alayhim (beneficiaries), and the mawquf (endowed property) itself. Assess each opinion's impact on these three.
Benefit includes both material and religious aspects.
3
Compare levels of benefit
Determine which opinion is more beneficial (anfa') for the waqf as a whole. This may require weighing short-term vs. long-term benefit.
Benefit to the waqf outweighs personal preference.
4
Prefer the beneficial opinion as mufta bihi
The opinion that yields greater benefit becomes the operative ruling for fatwa. The mufti should issue it as the relied-upon view.
Document the reasoning for transparency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آٹھواں اصول: انفع للوقف والا قول راجح ہوگا دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر کوئی قول واقف موقوف علیہم اور خودشیء موقوف کے لئے زیادہ نفع بخش ہو اور دوسرے قول میں یہ نفع موجود نہ ہوتو انفع للوقف والا قول راجح اور مفتی بہ ہوگا ۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٤٦)
Eighth Principle: The opinion beneficial for the waqf will be preponderant. Between two conflicting corrected opinions, if one opinion is more beneficial for the founder (waqif), the beneficiaries (mawquf alayhim), and the endowed property itself (shay' mawquf), and this benefit is not present in the other opinion, then the opinion that is beneficial for the waqf will be preponderant and the one to be issued as fatwa. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 146)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This is the eighth principle of preference among conflicting opinions. It applies specifically to issues of waqf (endowment). When two equally authenticated opinions conflict, the one that brings greater benefit to the waqf—including the donor, the beneficiaries, and the property itself—is to be preferred. This reflects the Shariah's objective of preserving and promoting the utility of endowments.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): A permanent endowment of property for charitable purposes, with the principal retained and benefits distributed.
انفع للوقف (anfa' lil-waqf): More beneficial for the waqf, considering all parties involved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the eighth principle, what does 'anfa' lil-waqf' mean?
A) The opinion that is easier for the people
B) The opinion that is more beneficial for the waqf, its founder, beneficiaries, and property
C) The opinion based on a strong hadith
D) The opinion that is more profitable for the mufti

Key Takeaway
The eighth principle of Rasm al-Mufti directs muftis to prefer the opinion most beneficial to the waqf, its founder, beneficiaries, and property.

Ninth Principle: Preferring Ease Over Hardship
Rule for preferring the opinion that provides ease to people

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ninth principle to choose between two equally authenticated opinions by identifying which provides ease (suhulat) to the people.

Core Idea
Between two valid opinions, the easier one aligns with the Shariah's temperament.

A mufti often encounters situations where two opinions are both authentically transmitted and equally supported by evidence. Which should he choose? This ninth principle from the classical manuals of fatwa gives a clear guidance: observe the Shariah's overall objective (maqasid) of facilitating ease, and prefer the opinion that brings comfort to the people. This principle is rooted in the Quranic promise that Allah intends ease, not hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting opinions
First, ensure both opinions are equally authenticated (musahhah) within the Hanafi school. Both must have proper chains and justification.
If one opinion is weaker in proof, the stronger one takes precedence regardless of ease.
2
Assess the impact on people
Evaluate each opinion: does it create ease (suhulat) or hardship (haraj) for the people who will practice it? Consider the general public, not just exceptional cases.
Hardship means significant difficulty in daily practice, not mere inconvenience.
3
Apply the principle of ease
Prefer the opinion that brings ease, because the Shariah's temperament (mizaj) is to facilitate. This is a recognised tarjih (preference) mechanism in Hanafi fatwa methodology.
This principle is applied after other tarjih factors (like textual strength) are equal.
4
Issue the fatwa accordingly
The mufti then gives the easier ruling, but must record that the other opinion is also valid for those who encounter exceptional hardship.
In some cases, the easier opinion may be the mufta bihi (operative ruling) of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نواں اصول بسہولت والا قول راجح ہوگا دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ایک قول میں لوگوں کے لئے سہولت اور آسانی ہو اور دوسرے قول میں لوگوں کے لئے حرج اور تنگی ہو تو شریعت کے مزاج و مذاق کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس میں آسانی ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى : ١٤٦ ، اصول الافتاء و آدابه: ٢٢٦)
Ninth Principle: The opinion with ease will be preponderant. Between two conflicting corrected opinions, if one opinion contains ease and facility for people, and the other contains hardship and difficulty for people, then, observing the temperament and taste of the Shariah, preference will be given to the opinion that contains ease. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 146; Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This ninth principle embodies the Shariah's objective (maqasid) of facilitating ease and removing hardship. When two opinions are equally authenticated, the mufti should prefer the one that is easier for the people to practice, as this aligns with the general character of Islamic law. This is based on the Quranic principle 'Allah intends ease for you, not hardship' (2:185).

Key Terms
سہولت (suhulat): Ease and facility in practicing a ruling, as opposed to hardship (haraj).
حرج (haraj): Hardship, difficulty, or constraint that makes practice burdensome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ninth principle, which opinion is to be preferred?
A) The opinion with greater textual support
B) The opinion that is easier for the people
C) The opinion that is stricter
D) The opinion of the majority of scholars

Key Takeaway
When two equally authenticated opinions conflict, the mufti should choose the one that brings ease, reflecting the Shariah's overarching objective of facilitation.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner

Tenth Principle: Preference for Stronger Narration
Rule for preferring opinion based on stronger hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the tenth principle of Rasm al-Mufti to resolve conflicting musahhah opinions by identifying which opinion is based on a sahih and mashhur hadith.

Core Idea
Prefer the fatwa backed by a sahih, mashhur hadith over one with weak or no evidence.

In Hanafi ifta, when two opinions are both considered sahih (correct) in the school, we need a rule to decide which one to give fatwa with. This tenth principle from Rasm al-Mufti provides a clear criterion: examine the underlying textual evidence. The opinion that relies on a sound and well-known hadith (sahih and mashhur) is preferred over one that has weak evidence or none at all. This lesson will help you identify and apply this crucial principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting musahhah opinions
First, confirm that both opinions are recognized as sahih (correct) within the Hanafi school, meaning each has been transmitted and accepted by later scholars.
Musahhah opinions are those marked as 'sahih' in later fatwa collections.
2
Examine the evidential basis of each opinion
Look at the primary evidence (dalil) behind each opinion. Check if it is based on a hadith, and if so, determine its authenticity (sahih) and level of transmission (mashhur or ahad).
A mashhur hadith is transmitted by at least three Companions but not reaching tawatur.
3
Apply the preference rule
Prefer the opinion whose basis is a sahih and mashhur hadith over the opinion that has no hadith basis or is based on a weak (da'if) hadith.
If both opinions have equally strong evidence, other principles may be consulted, but this principle gives a clear result when one side has stronger hadith support.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred opinion becomes the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for issuing fatwa. Document your reasoning, especially noting the strength of the hadith evidence.
This principle is one of several, so always check other relevant principles for comprehensive tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دسواں اصول: قومی دلیل پر مبنی قول رائج ہوگا
جب دو تعارض تصیح شدہ اقوال میں سے ایک قول کی بنیاد صحیح اور مشہور ومعروف حدیث پر ہو اور دوسرے قول کی بنیا دسرے سے کسی حدیث ہی پر نہ ہو یا کسی ضعیف سند والی حدیث پر اس کی بنیاد ہو تو ترجیح اس قول کو حاصل ہوگی جس کی بنیاد مضبوط دلیل پر ہو۔
شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٤٦،٩٤ ، اصول الافتاء و آدابه : ٢٢٦)
Tenth Principle: The opinion based on a strong evidence will be adopted. When between two conflicting corrected opinions, one opinion is based on a sound (sahih) and well-known (mashhur) hadith, and the other opinion is not based on any hadith at all or is based on a hadith with a weak chain, then preference will be given to the opinion whose basis is a strong evidence. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 146, 94; Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This tenth principle grounds preference in the strength of textual evidence. When two opinions are equally authenticated (musahhah), the one that relies on a sahih and mashhur hadith is preferred over one that relies on a weak hadith or no hadith. This ensures that fatwas are based on sound religious proofs, reflecting the importance of authentic hadith in Hanafi methodology.

Key Terms
قومی دلیل (qawmi dalil): A strong evidence, here referring specifically to a sound (sahih) and well-known (mashhur) hadith.
صحیح (sahih): A hadith with an uninterrupted chain of reliable narrators, free from defect.
مشہور (mashhur): Well-known (hadith), transmitted by at least three Companions but not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tenth principle, which type of evidence qualifies as 'qawmi dalil' for preferring an opinion?
A) Any hadith, regardless of authenticity
B) A sahih and mashhur hadith
C) A weak (da'if) hadith
D) A hadith that is mashhur but not necessarily sahih

Key Takeaway
When two equally sahih opinions conflict, the one supported by a sahih and mashhur hadith is preferred over one with weak or no hadith evidence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Eleventh Principle: Beneficial for the Poor in Zakat
Rule for mufti preference in zakat disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the eleventh principle (al-maslahah li al-fuqara') to resolve conflicting zakat opinions and identify when it governs.

Core Idea
In zakat, when scholarly opinions are equally strong, the one benefiting the poor takes precedence.

This lesson introduces a critical rasm al-mufti principle for zakat rulings. When a mufti faces two equally authoritative opinions, the maxim 'al-maslahah li al-fuqara'' directs him to choose the more beneficial for the poor. This ensures zakat fulfills its purpose of alleviating poverty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting opinions
When a mufti faces a zakat question with multiple positions, he must list both opinions and note their sources.
Both opinions must be from reliable transmissions.
2
Evaluate scholarly weight
Check if the opinions come from similar authority levels (e.g., both from Zahir al-Riwayah, or both from later works). If not, the stronger authority prevails and this principle does not apply.
If one opinion is from Imam Muhammad and the other from Imam Abu Yusuf, they are generally considered equal.
3
Determine which is more beneficial to the poor
Consider which ruling results in more wealth reaching the poor, or less hardship on the poor in fulfilling their zakat obligations.
Benefit is monetary or practical access to zakat funds.
4
Adopt that opinion as mufta bihi
Issue the fatwa according to the opinion that best serves the poor, and note the reasoning in the fatwa.
This principle ensures the maqsad of zakat is fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گیارہواں اصول: الفع للفقراء کا قول رائج ہوگا
زکوۃ کے باب میں اگر دو مختلف اقوال کو ایک ہی طرح کے الفاظ سے ترجیح دی گئی ہو اور ترجیح دینے والے فقہاء کی علمی حیثیت بھی برابر ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جو فقراء و مساکین کے لیے زیادہ مفید ہو۔ (اصول الافتاء وآدابه بتغيير: ٢٢٦)
Eleventh Principle: The opinion beneficial for the poor will be adopted. In the chapter of zakat, if two different opinions have been given preference with similar wording and the scholarly status of the preferring jurists is equal, then the opinion that is more beneficial for the poor and needy will have preference. (Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu with modification: 226)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This eleventh principle applies specifically to zakat rulings. When two opinions have been equally supported by scholars of similar standing, the mufti should choose the one that brings greater benefit to the poor (fuqara') and needy (masakin). This aligns with the objective of zakat, which is to fulfill the needs of the poor.

Key Terms
فقراء (fuqara'): The poor; one of the eligible categories for zakat recipients.
مساکین (masakin): The needy; extremely poor who may not have anything.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To which specific chapter does the eleventh principle apply?
A) Marriage
B) Zakat
C) Sales
D) Inheritance

Key Takeaway
When faced with two equally strong zakat opinions, the mufti adopts the one that brings greater benefit to the poor and needy.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Preferring the Opinion That Drops Hadd Penalties
Rule for preferring opinion that averts hadd penalties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Twelfth Principle of Rasm al-Mufti and apply it to resolve conflicting opinions regarding hadd penalties.

Core Idea
When opinions conflict equally, prefer the one that averts the hadd penalty.

This principle guides a mufti when faced with two equally supported but contradictory rulings on a matter involving a hadd penalty. The principle leverages the well-established rule that hudud are averted by doubts, ensuring mercy and caution in applying severe punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Locate two corrected opinions that contradict each other on a matter involving a hadd penalty. Confirm that the wording supporting each correction is similar and that the correcting scholars are of equal rank.
If the opinions are not equally supported, the usual tarjih (preference) rules apply first.
2
Determine which opinion drops the hadd
Examine the legal effect of each opinion. One opinion, if followed, would result in the hadd penalty being dropped (e.g., by requiring a condition that is absent or by interpreting the evidence leniently). The other opinion would uphold the penalty.
Remember: dropping the hadd does not mean acquitting the accused; it means applying a lesser penalty or no penalty due to doubt.
3
Apply the priority rule
Prefer the opinion that drops the hadd penalty. This is based on the general principle: 'Avert the hadd penalties by doubts' (idra'u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat).
This preference only holds when all other factors are equal.
4
Justify the ruling
Cite the legal basis: doubts (shubuhat) necessitate averting hudud. The chosen opinion is stronger because it aligns with this established maxim.
If the mufti chooses the opinion that upholds the penalty, the fatwa would be contrary to this rasm rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بارہواں اصول حدود کو ساقط کرنے والا قول راجح ہوگا متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح ایک ہی جیسے الفاظ سے کی جائے اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا مقام و مرتبہ بھی یکساں ہو تو ان میں سے جو قول حدود شرعیہ کو ساقط کرنے والا ہو اس کو دوسرے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، اس لیے کہ شبہات کی بناء پر حدود شرعیہ ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں۔ (اصول الافتاء وآدابه : ٢٢٦)
Twelfth Principle: The opinion that drops the hadd penalties will be preponderant. Between conflicting corrected opinions, if each opinion has been corrected with similar wording and the rank of the correcting scholars is equal, then whichever opinion is one that drops the prescribed penalties (hudud) will have preference over the other opinion, because prescribed penalties are dropped on the basis of doubts (shubuhat). (Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This twelfth principle applies to criminal law matters involving hadd penalties. When opinions conflict equally, the one that avoids or drops the hadd penalty is preferred. This follows the well-known hadith principle: 'Avert the hadd penalties by doubts' (idra'u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat). This ensures mercy and caution in applying severe punishments.

Key Terms
حدود شرعیہ (hudud shari'iyya): Prescribed punishments for specific offenses like theft, adultery, etc., as defined by Shariah.
شبہات (shubuhat): Doubts or uncertainties that prevent the application of hadd penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for applying the Twelfth Principle of Rasm al-Mufti?
A) Any conflicting opinions on any legal matter
B) Opinions must be equally corrected (same wording, equal scholar rank) and the matter involves a hadd penalty
C) Only when the mufti personally prefers leniency
D) Only when the accused is a repeat offender

Key Takeaway
When two equally supported opinions conflict on a hadd matter, prefer the one that drops the penalty based on the principle that hudud are averted by doubts.

Thirteenth Principle: Preference for Unlawful Over Lawful
Rule for preferring haram over halal in conflicting opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that when two equally authenticated opinions conflict on the permissibility of an action, the opinion that declares it haram is given preference, and you will be able to identify the supporting fiqh maxim.

Core Idea
When halal and haram conflict, the haram side is preferred due to caution.

This lesson presents a key principle from Rasm al-Mufti: when a mufti encounters two corrected opinions of equal strength—one declaring an act permissible (halal) and the other declaring it unlawful (haram)—the opinion indicating haram is given precedence. This is based on the well-known fiqh maxim that when halal and haram come together, the haram aspect is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Establish the scenario
Two conflicting corrected opinions exist. Both have been authenticated with similar wording and the correcting scholars are of equal rank.
2
Identify the two sides
One opinion says halal, the other says haram. The contrast is clear.
3
Apply the preference
The opinion declaring haram is given preference over the one declaring halal. This is a rule of caution in fatwa.
4
Recognize the underlying maxim
The rule is supported by the famous fiqh maxim: 'When halal and haram conflict, the haram side is preferred.'
This maxim is also frequently invoked in issues of doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیرہواں اصول : حرمت والا قول راجح ہوگا
متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح ایک ہی جیسے الفاظ سے کی جائے اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا مقام و مرتبہ بھی یکساں ہو تو ان میں سے جس قول میں حرمت کا پہلو ہو اس قول کو حلت والے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، کیوں کہ فقہ کا مشہور قاعدہ ہے: جب حلال و حرام کا اجتماع ہو جائے تو حرمت والے پہلو کو ترجیح دی جائے گی۔
اصول الافتاء و آدابه: ٢٢٦)
Thirteenth Principle: The opinion with prohibition will be preponderant. Between conflicting corrected opinions, if each opinion has been corrected with similar wording and the rank of the correcting scholars is equal, then the opinion that contains an aspect of prohibition (hurmat) will have preference over the opinion of permissibility (hillat), because the well-known rule of fiqh is: when halal and haram come together, the haram aspect is given preference. (Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This thirteenth principle applies when two equally authenticated opinions conflict on whether something is halal or haram. The opinion leaning toward haram is preferred, based on the established fiqh maxim: 'When halal and haram conflict, the haram side is given precedence.' This reflects caution in religious matters, avoiding that which may be unlawful.

Key Terms
حرمت (hurmat): The quality of being unlawful (haram) in Shariah.
حلت (hillat): Permissibility or lawfulness (halal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Acts are judged by intentions'
B) 'When halal and haram conflict, the haram is preferred'
C) 'Certainty is not removed by doubt'
D) 'Hardship brings ease'

Key Takeaway
When two equally authenticated opinions conflict on halal and haram, the opinion preferring haram must be given precedence to safeguard against prohibited acts.

Tenth Principle: Stronger Evidence Prevails
Stating a principle for preferring rulings based on evidence strength

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the tenth principle to prefer one corrected saying over another based on the strength of its hadith evidence.

Core Idea
When corrected sayings conflict, the one backed by a sound, well-known hadith prevails.

A mufti often faces multiple transmitted rulings that have been deemed correct (musahhah) by later scholars. When these sayings appear contradictory, on what basis should he choose? This lesson introduces the tenth principle of rasm al-mufti: the saying supported by a stronger evidence—specifically a sahih or mashhur hadith—is preferred over one that lacks such support or relies on a weak hadith. This ensures fatwas are built on the most authentic proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting corrected sayings
First, confirm that you have two or more statements that have been corrected (musahhah) and that they conflict in their ruling for the same case.
Corrected sayings are those approved in later Hanafi works; not all transmitted sayings qualify.
2
Examine the basis of each saying
Determine what proof (dalil) each saying is built upon. Is it a hadith? If yes, what is its level of authenticity (sahih, hasan, da'if, etc.)? Is it well-known (mashhur)?
The principle specifically compares hadith-based evidence, not qiyas or other proofs.
3
Check if one basis is a sound, well-known hadith
If one saying rests on a sahih and mashhur hadith, while the other either has no hadith basis or relies on a weak (da'if) hadith, the first saying is stronger.
If both sayings have sound hadiths, other tarjih principles apply.
4
Apply the principle to prefer the stronger-evidence saying
Give preference to the saying whose basis is a strong (sound and well-known) hadith. This is the mufta bihi ruling.
This principle is part of the mufti's toolkit for resolving ta'arud among musahhah aqwal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب دو تعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے ایک قول کی بنیاد صحیح اور مشہور ومعروف حدیث پر ہو اور دوسرے قول کی بنیاد دوسرے سے کسی حدیث ہی پر نہ ہو یا کسی ضعیف سند والی حدیث پر اس کی بنیاد ہو تو ترجیح اس قول کو حاصل ہوگی جس کی بنیاد مضبوط دلیل پر ہو۔
When among two conflicting corrected sayings, the basis of one saying is a sound and well-known hadith, and the basis of the other saying is not upon any hadith at all or its basis is upon a hadith with a weak chain, then preference will be given to the saying whose basis is a strong proof.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage states the tenth principle of mufti methodology: when two conflicting fatwas have been corrected (i.e., deemed valid for practice), preference is given to the one supported by a stronger evidence. The evidence in question is a hadith that is authentic (sahih) and well-known (mashhur). If the opposing view lacks any hadith basis or relies on a weak (da'if) hadith, the stronger-evidence view is preferred. This is because fiqh rulings are built on proofs, and a stronger proof yields a stronger ruling.

Key Terms
تعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال (ta'āruḍ muṣaḥḥaḥ aqwāl): Two or more transmitted rulings that have been independently deemed correct by later scholars, yet apparently contradict each other

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tenth principle, which saying is preferred when two corrected sayings conflict?
A) The saying that is easier for the public
B) The saying that is based on a sound and well-known hadith
C) The saying that is from a later jurist
D) The saying that is more cautious

Key Takeaway
When two corrected sayings conflict, the mufti must prefer the one built on a sound, well-known hadith over one lacking such evidence.

The 11th Principle: Preferring Benefit to the Poor in Zakat
Stating a principle for preferring rulings that benefit the poor in zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the 11th principle of Rasm al-Mufti to prefer the ruling more beneficial to the poor in zakat when equal authorities conflict.

Core Idea
When zakat sayings conflict equally, prefer what benefits the poor — zakat is their right.

In the chapter of zakat, fuqaha sometimes give equal weight to conflicting rulings. This principle from Rasm al-Mufti resolves that deadlock by instructing the mufti to prefer the saying that maximizes benefit for the poor and needy (fuqarā’ wa masākīn). This ensures the maqasid (objectives) of zakat are fulfilled, as zakat is fundamentally a right of the poor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Ensure there are two sayings (aqwal) on the zakat issue that are equally preferred (i.e., both have been endorsed with similar wording by scholars of equal rank).
The principle only applies when the authorities are equal in rank and the phrasing is similar.
2
Verify the discipline
Confirm that the dispute falls within the chapter of zakat. This principle does not apply to other chapters of fiqh.
The source explicitly states 'fi bab al-zakat'.
3
Assess benefit to the poor
Determine which of the two sayings provides greater benefit (more maslahah) to the poor and needy (fuqarā’ wa masākīn).
Consider both material benefit and ease of access to zakat funds.
4
Apply preference
Choose the saying that best serves the poor. This becomes the mufta bihi (operative opinion) for that case.
Tarjih (preference) is based on the maqsad of zakat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زکوۃ کے باب میں اگر دو مختلف اقوال کو ایک ہی طرح کے الفاظ سے ترجیح دی گئی ہو اور ترجیح دینے والے فقہاء کی علمی حیثیت بھی برابر ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جو فقراء و مساکین کے لیے زیادہ مفید ہو۔
In the chapter of zakat, if two different sayings have been given preference with similar wording and the scholarly status of the preferring jurists is also equal, then preference will be given to that saying which is more beneficial for the poor and needy.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh principle: in zakat matters, when two conflicting yet equally corrected rulings are both endorsed by scholars of equal rank using identical phrasing, the ruling that provides greater benefit to the poor and needy (fuqara' wa masakin) is preferred. This is because zakat is fundamentally a right of the poor, and the maqasid (objectives) of Shari'ah favor easing their situation.

Key Terms
فقراء و مساکین (fuqarā' wa masākīn): The poor and needy, the primary recipients of zakat

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When one saying is based on a stronger hadith
B) In zakat, when two sayings are equally preferred and scholars equal
C) When the saying is from Imam Abu Hanifa
D) When the saying avoids hardship

Key Takeaway
In zakat, when scholars equally endorse conflicting rulings, the mufti must prefer the one that benefits the poor and needy.

Twelfth Principle: Dropping Hudud is Preferred
Stating a principle for preferring rulings that avert hudud penalties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that favours dropping hudud to resolve conflicting corrected sayings in fatwa.

Core Idea
When rulings conflict equally, the one that drops a hadd penalty is preferred because hudud drop with doubts.

The mufti often faces conflicting sayings that are equally authoritative. This principle provides a clear preference: choose the saying that avoids the harsh hadd penalty. This reflects Shari'ah's inclination to avert hudud in cases of doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify conflicting corrected sayings
Locate the two or more sayings that have been corrected (tasheeh) by scholars of similar wording and rank.
The correction wording and scholar rank must be equal for this principle to apply.
2
Determine if one saying drops a hadd
Check if any of the conflicting sayings results in the cancellation or non-application of a prescribed hadd penalty (e.g., amputation, stoning, lashes).
If none of the sayings involves a hadd, this principle may not apply.
3
Apply preference
Prefer the saying that drops the hadd over the one that imposes it.
The reason is the known maxim: hudud are averted by doubts.
4
Document the reasoning
In your fatwa, cite this principle and the underlying doubt that caused the preference.
The doubt (shubha) must be legitimate and not manufactured.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح ایک ہی جیسے الفاظ سے کی جائے اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا مقام و مرتبہ بھی یکساں ہو تو ان میں سے جو قول حدود شرعیہ کو ساقط کرنے والا ہو اس کو دوسرے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، اس لیے کہ شبہات کی بناء پر حدود شرعیہ ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں۔
Among conflicting corrected sayings, if each saying has been corrected with similar wording and the status and rank of the correcting scholars is also equal, then among them the saying that drops the prescribed penalties (hudud) will be given preference over the other saying, because prescribed penalties are dropped on the basis of doubts.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the twelfth principle: when two corrected sayings are equally endorsed by scholars of equal rank using identical phrasing, the ruling that results in dropping a hadd penalty (such as amputation, stoning, or lashes for zina, theft, etc.) is preferred. The reason is the well-known fiqh maxim that hudud are averted by doubts (shubahat). Since Shari'ah aims to avoid harsh penalties when uncertainties exist, the more lenient ruling that avoids the penalty is chosen.

Key Terms
حدود شرعیہ (ḥudūd shar'iyyah): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Hudud
C) Qisas
D) All types of penalties

Key Takeaway
Prefer the ruling that drops a hadd when equally corrected sayings conflict, because hudud are averted by doubts.

13th Principle: Prohibition Outweighs Permissibility
Stating a principle for preferring prohibition over permissibility in conflicting sayings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that prohibition outweighs permissibility when conflicting corrected sayings are equal in wording and scholar rank.

Core Idea
When halal and haram conflict, prohibition is preferred – a principle of caution in fatwa.

As a mufti, you may encounter two equally reliable sayings from past scholars on the same issue. How do you decide? The thirteenth principle gives clear guidance: when both sayings are corrected with equal wording and from scholars of equal rank, the one leaning towards prohibition is given precedence. This aligns with the maxim 'when halal and haram coincide, prohibition is given preference', reflecting the Hanafi commitment to ihtiyat (precaution).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting sayings
Recognize that there are two equally corrected sayings on a matter, each with similar authentication.
These sayings must be of equal evidentiary value.
2
Verify equality conditions
Check that both sayings are corrected with similar wording and by scholars of equal rank.
If one saying is from a higher-ranked scholar, that may override this principle.
3
Apply the preference rule
After confirming equality, choose the saying that declares prohibition over permissibility.
The rule applies even if both sayings appear equally plausible.
4
Invoke the maxim
Cite the well-known fiqh maxim: 'When halal and haram coincide, prohibition is given precedence.'
This maxim is used to justify the preference.
5
Understand the rationale
The preference is based on caution (ihtiyat) to avoid potential sin or harm.
This reflects the Hanafi approach of erring on the side of prohibition when doubt exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح ایک ہی جیسے الفاظ سے کی جائے اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا مقام و مرتبہ بھی یکساں ہو تو ان میں سے جس قول میں حرمت کا پہلو ہو اس قول کو حلت والے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، کیوں کہ فقہ کا مشہور قاعدہ ہے: جب حلال و حرام کا اجتماع ہو جائے تو حرمت والے پہلو کو ترجیح دی جائے گی۔
Among conflicting corrected sayings, if each saying has been corrected with similar wording and the status and rank of the correcting scholars is also equal, then among them the saying that has the aspect of prohibition will be given preference over the saying of permissibility, because the well-known maxim of fiqh is: When halal and haram come together, the aspect of prohibition is given preference.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the thirteenth principle: when two equally corrected rulings are endorsed by scholars of equal rank, the one that declares something prohibited (haram) is preferred over the one that declares it permissible (halal). This is based on the famous legal maxim: 'When halal and haram coincide, the aspect of prohibition is given preference.' The rationale is caution (ihtiyat) and avoiding potential harm.

Key Terms
حلال و حرام (ḥalāl wa ḥarām): Permissible and forbidden; the two categories of legal value

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Fourteenth Principle: Preferring the Saying Based on Maslahah and Custom
Stating a principle for preferring rulings based on maslahah and custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fourteenth principle of tarjih to prefer a mufta bihi saying based on maslahah and custom when corrected sayings are equivalent.

Core Idea
When corrected rulings are equal, the one grounded in public interest and custom takes precedence.

This lesson introduces a key principle from the Hanafi usul al-iftaa tradition: when two corrected narrations are equally endorsed, the mufti must prefer the one that serves public interest (maslahah) or aligns with prevailing custom ('urf). The authority cited from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir quoting al-Bazzaziyyah emphasizes the role of maslahah in tarjih. This principle reflects the Hanafi recognition that custom and benefit have weight in preferring one transmitted ruling over another, as long as they do not contradict clear nass.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of conflict
Confirm that there are two corrected sayings with equal phrasing and the rank of the correcting scholars is identical. This establishes a true ta'arud (conflict) requiring tarjih.
2
Apply the preference principle
Among the equally corrected sayings, give preference (tarjih) to the saying that is based on maslahah (public interest) or 'urf (custom). The mufti should adopt the saying that contains a benefit for the community.
Reference from al-Ashbah: the mufti gives fatwa on the saying that has maslahah.
3
Recognize the scope and exceptions
This principle applies only when the corrected sayings are equivalent and neither contradicts a clear nass (text). If a custom or maslahah conflicts with a definitive proof (Quran, Sunnah), the nass overrides.
The maxim 'العادة محكمة' is qualified: custom contrary to nass is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح یکساں الفاظ سے کی گئی ہو اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا رتبہ بھی برابر ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس کی بنیاد مصلحت اور عرف وغیرہ پر ہو، چنانچہ الاشباہ میں بزازیہ کے حوالہ سے منقول ہے کہ مفتی اس قول پر فتوی دے گا جس میں کوئی مصلحت ہو۔
Among two conflicting corrected sayings, if each saying has been corrected with similar wording and the rank of the correcting scholars is also equal, then preference will be given to that saying whose basis is maslahah (public interest) and custom ('urf), etc. Accordingly, it is narrated in al-Ashbah quoting al-Bazzaziyyah that the mufti will give fatwa according to the saying in which there is some maslahah.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents the fourteenth principle: when two corrected rulings are equivalent in endorsement, the one grounded in public interest (maslahah) and custom ('urf) is preferred. The authority cited includes al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, quoting al-Bazzaziyyah, stating that the mufti should adopt the ruling that contains maslahah. This reflects the Hanafi recognition of custom and public interest as secondary sources that can influence tarjih.

Key Terms
مصلحت (maṣlaḥah): Public interest or benefit, a consideration that influences tarjih
عرف ('urf): Custom or established practice of the people

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for preferring a saying according to the fourteenth principle?
A) The saying is from a later scholar
B) The saying is based on general practice or public interest
C) The saying is easier to implement
D) The saying is supported by a hadith

Key Takeaway
In tarjih, when corrected rulings are equal, the one based on maslahah and custom is preferred, provided it does not contradict nass.

The Fourteenth Principle: Preferring the Ruling Based on Maslahah
Explains the fourteenth principle with important nuance from later scholarship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule of preferring a maslahah-based ruling among equally authenticated opinions and apply it, while identifying when preference factors conflict and explaining the mufti's reliance on dhawq and malakah.

Core Idea
When rulings are equally authenticated, choose the one serving maslahah—unless preference factors conflict, then rely on trained judgment.

In mufti methodology, preference among conflicting authenticated rulings is guided by principles. This lesson presents the fourteenth principle: prefer the maslahah-based ruling when all else is equal. But as Mufti Taqi 'Uthmani explains, the preference factors themselves can conflict, and then no fixed rule suffices—the mufti must draw on his sound juristic taste (dhawq sahih) and ingrained faculty (malakah fiqhiyyah). This lesson unpacks both the rule and its crucial nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
State the rule: when two conflicting rulings are equally authenticated (same wording, same scholars' rank), prefer the one based on maslahah and custom.
The principle is from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, supported by al-Ashbah.
2
Understand the Condition
Note that the rule applies only when authentication is equal. If one ruling has stronger evidence (e.g., in Zahir al-Riwayah), other factors may override.
Equal authentication is key; without it, other tarjih rules apply.
3
Recognize the Nuance
Mufti Taqi 'Uthmani warns that preference factors (wujuh al-tarjih) can conflict—e.g., one ruling being in Zahir al-Riwayah and another being Imam Abu Hanifa's own saying.
When factors conflict, no universal rule works.
4
Know the Fallback
In case of conflicting factors, the mufti relies on his dhawq sahih and malakah fiqhiyyah—trained judgment developed through deep study.
This is not arbitrary; it is expertise.
5
Apply in Practice
The mufti may choose precaution (sadd al-dhara'i') or ease (taysir) based on circumstances, but always within his trained discernment.
Practical examples: widespread issues favor ease; risky matters favor precaution.

يم المفتى فى حل من شي عقود رسم المف
چودہواں اصول مصلحت پر مبنی قول راج ہوگا
دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح یکساں الفاظ سے کی گئی ہو اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا رتبہ بھی برابر ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس کی بنیاد مصلحت اور عرف وغیرہ پر ہو، چنانچہ الاشباہ میں بزازیہ کے حوالہ سے منقول ہے کہ مفتی اس قول پر فتوی دے گا جس میں کوئی مصلحت ہو۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٦٩) مشائخ کی ترجیحات میں تطبیق سے متعلق ایک اہم فائدہ
شیخ الاسلام حضرت مفتی تقی عثمانی صاحب اپنی مایہ ناز کتاب اصول الافتاء وآدابه میں فرماتے ہیں کہ ان تمام وجوہ ترجیح کو فقہاء نے بیان کیا ہے اور وہ ایک قول کو دوسرے قول پر ترجیح دینے کے لیے ان کا استعمال کرتے رہتے ہیں، لیکن یہ سب ایسے قواعد کلیہ نہیں ہیں کہ ان پر تمام حالات میں عمل کیا جاسکے، اس لئے کہ بسا اوقات خودان مرجحات کے ما بین تعارض ہو جاتا ہے، بایں طور کہ اسباب ترجیح میں سے کوئی سبب ایک قول کی ترجیح چاہتا ہے اور دوسرا سبب دوسرے قول کی ترجیح چاہتا ہے ( مثلا کسی قول کا ظاہر الروایہ میں ہوتا اس کی ترجیح کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اور اس کے مقابل دوسرے قول کا امام صاحب کا قول ہونا اس قول کی ترجیح کا تقاضا کرتا ہے ، اب کس سبب کی بنیاد پر ان اقوال کو ترجیح دی جائے گی یہ ایک مشکل امر ہے) لہذا اس صورت میں ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ بیان کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے جس پر ہر جگہ عمل کیا جا سکے، تو ایسی مثالوں میں معاملہ مفتی کے ذوق صحیح اور ملکہ فقہیہ کے سپر د کر دیا جاتا ہے جو ان متعارض وجوہ ترجیح میں سے ایک کا انتخاب کر لیتا ہے، بسا اوقات مفتی اس امر کی ضرورت محسوس کرتے ہیں کہ سد ذرائع ہو تو و و احتیاط والے قول پر فتوی دیتے ہیں اور کبھی مفتی کے سامنے ایسا مسئلہ آتا ہے جس میں ابتلاء عام ہوتا ہے تو وہ اس قول پر عمل کرتے ہیں جس میں لوگوں کے لیے سہولت ہوتی ہے۔ (اصول الافتاء و آدابه: ٢٢٦)
Fourteenth principle: A ruling based on maslahah will be preferred. Among two conflicting authenticated statements, if each statement has been authenticated with identical wording and the status of the authenticating scholars is equal, then preference will be given to the statement whose foundation is maslahah and custom (urf), etc. Thus, it is narrated from al-Ashbah via al-Bazzaziyyah that the mufti will give fatwa on the statement in which there is some maslahah. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 169) An important benefit regarding the application of the preferences of the mashayikh: Shaykh al-Islam Mufti Taqi 'Uthmani says in his masterpiece Usul al-Ifta' wa Adabuh: All these reasons for preference have been mentioned by the jurists, and they use them to prefer one statement over another. However, these are not all universal principles that can be applied in all situations, because sometimes these very preferences conflict with each other, in that one cause of preference demands the preference of one statement and another cause demands the preference of the other statement (for example, a statement being in Zahir al-Riwayah demands its preference, while the other statement being the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa himself demands its preference. Now on which basis should these statements be preferred? This is a difficult matter). Therefore, in such a case, it is not possible to state a universal principle that can be applied everywhere. So in such examples, the matter is left to the mufti's sound taste (dhawq sahih) and juristic faculty (malakah fiqhiyyah), which selects one of these conflicting reasons for preference. Sometimes the mufti feels the need to block the means (sadd al-dhara'i') and gives fatwa on the precautionary statement, and sometimes the mufti faces a problem that is widespread among people, then he acts on the statement that contains ease for the people. (Usul al-Ifta' wa Adabuh: 226)
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents the fourteenth principle of mufti's methodology: when two conflicting rulings have been equally authenticated (by scholars of similar rank and using identical terms of authentication), the mufti should prefer the one that is based on public interest (maslahah) and custom (urf). The passage cites al-Ashbah via al-Bazzaziyyah to support this rule. Then Mufti Taqi 'Uthmani provides an important refinement: these preference factors (wujuh al-tarjih) are not universal rules that apply in all cases. Sometimes the preference factors themselves conflict, e.g., one statement is in Zahir al-Riwayah (generally stronger) while the other is the personal saying of Imam Abu Hanifa (which carries special weight). In such cases, no fixed rule can cover all situations. Instead, the mufti must rely on his sound juristic taste (dhawq sahih) and juristic faculty (malakah fiqhiyyah) to choose. At times, he may opt for the precautionary ruling (to block evil means), and at other times, when the issue is widespread, he may choose the easier opinion for the people. This passage teaches that ifta' is not mechanical rule-application but requires informed judgment.

Key Terms
مصلحت (maslahah): Public interest or benefit that the Law considers. Here it is a criterion for preferring one ruling over another when other factors are equal.
ذوق صحیح (dhawq sahih): The sound juristic taste of the mufti, developed through deep study of fiqh, that allows him to discern the correct preference when textual criteria conflict.
ملکہ فقہیہ (malakah fiqhiyyah): The juristic faculty or ingrained expertise in fiqh that enables a mufti to weigh conflicting evidences and apply the correct ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when two equally authenticated rulings conflict and the preference factors also conflict, what does the mufti rely on to choose the correct ruling?
A) A universal rule that works in all cases
B) The opinion of a single later authority
C) His sound juristic taste and faculty (dhawq sahih and malakah fiqhiyyah)
D) The ruling that is easiest for the people in all cases

Key Takeaway
The mufti's role is not mechanical; when preference factors conflict, his trained judgment (dhawq and malakah) becomes the decisive tool.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Fourth Principle: Fatwa Only from Reliable Books
Explains the fourth principle of fatwa: giving fatwa only from reliable books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria for a reliable Hanafi fatwa source and state Ibn 'Abidin's warning against using certain later works for direct fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must only give fatwa from books the school has recognized as reliable; not every Hanafi book is fit for fatwa.

This fourth principle of fatwa highlights a crucial distinction: some Hanafi books compile all types of opinions without differentiation, while others restrict themselves to sound, relied-upon positions. The mufti must know which category his source belongs to. Ibn 'Abidin issues a strong warning: using concise later works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar without verification often leads to unreliable fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understanding the two categories of Hanafi books
Identify that some books (e.g., al-Mabsut) collect all opinions, while others (e.g., al-Hidayah) only transmit Zahir al-Riwayah and sound opinions.
The passage distinguishes between comprehensive compilations and selective reliable works.
2
Recognizing the necessity of knowing a book's status
Understand that the mufti must know the scholarly standing of the book he uses; it is not enough that it was written by a Hanafi author.
Ibn 'Abidin emphasizes that books like Sharh al-Niqayah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar are not automatically reliable.
3
Learning Ibn 'Abidin's specific warning
Learn that Ibn 'Abidin singles out certain later works as unreliable due to extreme brevity, textual errors, and presenting marjuh opinions as rajih.
This warning applies to most who refer to just one such book.
4
Internalizing the consequence
Understand that fatwa from an unreliable source has no legal weight (la i'tibara lahu).
The mufti must either use a reliable work or cross-check with one.

سم المفتى فى حل مباد
چوتھا اصول
معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا
شن عقود رسم المفى ا
فقہ حنفی کی بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن میں ظاہر الروایہ اور غیر ظاہر الروایہ، اقوی اور قوی صحیح اور غیر صحیح، راج اور غیر راج الغرض ہر قسم کے اقوال کو جمع کر دیا گیا ہے، ان کتابوں میں کوئی ایسی علامت بھی مذکور نہیں ہے جس سے ان اقوال کے مابین صحت و فساد اور قوت و ضعف کے اعتبار سے تمیز کیا جا سکے، اس کے برعکس بعض کتابیں ایسی بھی ہیں جن کے مصنفین نے اس بات کا التزام کیا ہے کہ وہ اپنی کتابوں میں صرف ظاہر الروایہ اور مذہب کے صحیح و معتمد قول کو نقل کرتے ہیں اور جہاں ضعیف قول لکھنے کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے تو اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ بھی کر دیتے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دیتے وقت مفتی کے لئے اس بات سے واقف ہونا انتہائی ضروری ہے کہ جس کتاب سے وہ فتوی دے رہا ہے فقہ حنفی میں اس کا مقام و مرتبہ کیا ہے؟ علماء نے اس کو معتبر کتابوں میں شمار کیا ہے یا اسے غیر معتبر قرار دیا ہے۔
علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں: میں کہتا ہوں کہ جب تم اس بات کو جان لیے ہو کہ راجح قول کی پیروی کرنا واجب ہے اور ترجیح دینے والوں کے احوال سے بھی واقف ہو چکے ہو، تو یہ بھی جان لو کہ ہمارے زمانہ کے اکثر لوگ جو متاخرین کی کتابوں میں سے محض ایک کتاب کی طرف مراجعت کر کے فتوی دید یتے ہیں تو اس فتوی کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے، خاص طور سے جب وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہو، جیسے کہ علامہ قہستانی کی شرح النقایه ،علامہ حصکفی کی الدرالمختار ،علامہ ابن نجیم کی الاشباہ والنظائر اور ان جیسی کتابیں، کیوں کہ عبارتوں کے انتہائی مختصر ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ کتابیں ایک معمہ بن گئی ہیں، نیز ان کتابوں میں بہت سے مقامات پر عبارت نقل کرنے میں غلطی بھی ہوئی ہے، ( بعض مسائل میں ) مرجوح قول کو راجح قرار دیا گیا ہے، بلکہ ان اقوال کو بھی راج قرار دیا گیا ہے جس کا ہمارے مذہب کے ائمہ میں سے کوئی بھی قائل نہیں ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی ۵۴۰)
Fourth principle: Giving fatwa from reliable books. Some Hanafi books contain all types of statements: Zahir al-Riwayah and non-Zahir, stronger and strong, sound and unsound, preferred and non-preferred — in short, every kind of statement has been collected in them. In these books, no such sign is mentioned by which these statements can be distinguished in terms of soundness and corruption, strength and weakness. In contrast, there are some books whose authors have committed to transmitting only the Zahir al-Riwayah and the sound, relied-upon statements of the school, and wherever there is a need to write a weak statement, they also indicate its weakness. Therefore, when giving fatwa, it is extremely necessary for the mufti to know what rank and status the book from which he is giving fatwa has in Hanafi fiqh. Have the scholars counted it among the reliable books or have they declared it unreliable? 'Allamah Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami says: I say: when you have known that following the preferred (rajih) statement is obligatory and you have become aware of the conditions of those who give preference, then also know that most people of our time who give fatwa by referring to just one book from among the later scholars' books — their fatwa has no weight, especially when that book is unreliable, such as 'Allamah Quhistani's Sharh al-Niqayah, 'Allamah al-Haskafi's al-Durr al-Mukhtar, 'Allamah Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, and similar books. Because due to extreme brevity of expressions, these books have become an enigma. Also, in many places in these books, errors have occurred in transmitting the text. In some issues, the non-preferred (marjuh) statement has been declared preferred, rather statements have been preferred that none of the imams of our school actually held. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 540)
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth principle: the mufti must give fatwa only from reliable books. It distinguishes two categories of Hanafi books: (1) comprehensive compilations that include all kinds of rulings (sound and weak, Zahir al-Riwayah and non-Zahir) without distinction, making them unreliable for direct fatwa; (2) selective works that restrict themselves to the relied-upon, sound positions of the school, and when they mention a weak opinion, they flag it. The mufti must know which category his source belongs to. Ibn 'Abidin then issues a strong warning: most contemporaries who take fatwa from just one book from the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) — such as Sharh al-Niqayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir (note: these are prominent but considered unreliable for direct fatwa due to their brevity and errors) — their fatwa has no legal weight. He points out that these books, due to extreme conciseness, are like puzzles, contain textual errors, and sometimes present marjuh (outweighed) opinions as rajih (preferred), or even opinions that no Hanafi imam ever held. This is a critical reminder for muftis: not every book authored by a Hanafi scholar is automatically reliable for fatwa; one must know the scholarly consensus on the reliability of the source.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The manifest transmissions from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) as compiled in the six major works of Imam Muhammad. These have the highest authority in the school.
معتبر کتاب (mu'tabar kitab): A book that is considered reliable by the scholars of the school, meaning it contains only relied-upon positions or clearly distinguishes weak opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn 'Abidin, why are books like al-Durr al-Mukhtar and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir considered unreliable for giving fatwa directly?
A) They are too long and hard to use
B) They contain only weak opinions
C) They are extremely brief, prone to errors, and sometimes present wrong opinions as preferred
D) They were not written by Hanafi scholars

Key Takeaway
Fatwa must be based on books that the school has recognized as reliable; using an unreliable book invalidates the fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Fourth Principle: Fatwa from Reliable Books
Rasm al-mufti rule on book reliability with Ibn Abidin's commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two categories of Hanafi fiqh books and apply Ibn Abidin's criteria to evaluate a book's reliability for fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must verify a book's scholarly status before using it for fatwa; not all Hanafi books are equally reliable.

A mufti cannot simply open any Hanafi book and issue a ruling. The school's extensive literature varies widely in reliability: some works indiscriminately collect all narrations, while others carefully transmit only the authoritative positions. Knowing the difference is a core responsibility of the mufti. In this lesson, we explore the fourth principle of Rasm al-Mufti, which demands that fatwas be derived from reliable books, and we examine Ibn Abidin's critical warning against depending solely on late abbreviated works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of Hanafi fiqh books
First, distinguish between books that compile all types of narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah and others, strong and weak) without markers, and those whose authors commit to transmitting only the relied-upon positions and flag weak narrations.
The passage gives examples of the second category but not the first. Think of works like al-Mabsut and al-Hidayah as representative of the reliable type.
2
Determine which category your chosen book belongs to
Check the author's introduction or the scholarly consensus about the book. Does it claim to transmit only Zahir al-Riwayah and the mu'tamad? Or does it mix everything without distinction?
For instance, al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a later work that, despite its fame, belongs to the problematic category per Ibn Abidin.
3
Verify the book's reputation among Hanafi scholars
Consult the works of Hanafi scholars (e.g., Ibn Abidin, al-Haskafi) to see if they consider the book mu'tabar (reliable) for fatwa.
The passage cites Ibn Abidin explicitly naming al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, and Sharh al-Nuqaya as unreliable.
4
Apply Ibn Abidin's warning against sole reliance on a single late work
Even if a book is famous, if it is known to have errors and extreme brevity, it should not be the sole source. Cross-reference with a more reliable primary text.
Ibn Abidin warns that such books may contain textual errors, present outweighed opinions as preferable, and even attribute statements to imams that they never made.
5
Cross-reference the ruling with other reliable sources
Before issuing a fatwa, confirm the ruling in at least one of the foundational books of the madhhab (e.g., al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, or al-Hidayah) to ensure it reflects the rajih position.
This step safeguards against errors in transmission and ensures the fatwa aligns with the established school position.

چوتھا اصول
معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا
فقہ حنفی کی بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن میں ظاہر الروایہ اور غیر ظاہر الروایہ، اقوی اور قوی صحیح اور غیر صحیح، راج اور غیر راج الغرض ہر قسم کے اقوال کو جمع کر دیا گیا ہے، ان کتابوں میں کوئی ایسی علامت بھی مذکور نہیں ہے جس سے ان اقوال کے مابین صحت و فساد اور قوت و ضعف کے اعتبار سے تمیز کیا جا سکے، اس کے برعکس بعض کتابیں ایسی بھی ہیں جن کے مصنفین نے اس بات کا التزام کیا ہے کہ وہ اپنی کتابوں میں صرف ظاہر الروایہ اور مذہب کے صحیح و معتمد قول کو نقل کرتے ہیں اور جہاں ضعیف قول لکھنے کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے تو اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ بھی کر دیتے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دیتے وقت مفتی کے لئے اس بات سے واقف ہونا انتہائی ضروری ہے کہ جس کتاب سے وہ فتوی دے رہا ہے فقہ حنفی میں اس کا مقام و مرتبہ کیا ہے؟ علماء نے اس کو معتبر کتابوں میں شمار کیا ہے یا اسے غیر معتبر قرار دیا ہے۔
علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں: میں کہتا ہوں کہ جب تم اس بات کو جان لیے ہو کہ راجح قول کی پیروی کرنا واجب ہے اور ترجیح دینے والوں کے احوال سے بھی واقف ہو چکے ہو، تو یہ بھی جان لو کہ ہمارے زمانہ کے اکثر لوگ جو متاخرین کی کتابوں میں سے محض ایک کتاب کی طرف مراجعت کر کے فتوی دید یتے ہیں تو اس فتوی کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے، خاص طور سے جب وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہو، جیسے کہ علامہ قہستانی کی شرح النقایه ،علامہ حصکفی کی الدرالمختار ،علامہ ابن نجیم کی الاشباہ والنظائر اور ان جیسی کتابیں، کیوں کہ عبارتوں کے انتہائی مختصر ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ کتابیں ایک معمہ بن گئی ہیں، نیز ان کتابوں میں بہت سے مقامات پر عبارت نقل کرنے میں غلطی بھی ہوئی ہے، ( بعض مسائل میں ) مرجوح قول کو راجح قرار دیا گیا ہے، بلکہ ان اقوال کو بھی راج قرار دیا گیا ہے جس کا ہمارے مذہب کے ائمہ میں سے کوئی بھی قائل نہیں ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی ۵۴۰)
Fourth Principle: Giving fatwa from reliable books. Among the Hanafi fiqh books are those that contain all kinds of statements: Zahir al-Riwayah and non-Zahir al-Riwayah, stronger and strong, correct and incorrect, preferable and non-preferable; in these books there is no sign by which one can distinguish between them in terms of soundness and weakness, strength and weakness. On the contrary, there are books whose authors have committed to only transmitting Zahir al-Riwayah and the correct, relied-upon statement of the madhhab, and where a weak statement needs to be written they indicate its weakness. Therefore, when giving fatwa it is extremely necessary for the mufti to know what the rank and status of the book from which he is giving fatwa is in the Hanafi fiqh: have the scholars counted it among the reliable books or declared it unreliable? Allamah Ibn Abidin al-Shami says: I say: when you have known that following the preferred (rajih) statement is obligatory and you have become aware of the conditions of those who give preference, then know also that most people of our time who give fatwa by referring to only one book among the later works—that fatwa has no validity, especially when the book is unreliable, like Allamah Quhistani's Sharh al-Nuqaya, Allamah Haskafi's al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Allamah Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir and similar books, because due to extreme brevity these books have become an enigma, and also in many places there are errors in transmitting expressions, and (in some issues) the outweighed statement has been considered preferable, even statements that none of the imams of our madhhab held have been considered preferable. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, p.540)
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning the fourth principle: the necessity of relying on reliable books when issuing fatwas. The author first distinguishes two categories of Hanafi fiqh works: (1) compilations that indiscriminately gather all types of narrations—Zahir al-Riwayah and otherwise, strong and weak, correct and incorrect—without any markers for distinction; (2) books whose authors deliberately transmit only the Zahir al-Riwayah and the sound, relied-upon (mu'tamad) positions of the madhhab, and who flag any weak narrations they include. The mufti must know which category a given book belongs to. The passage then quotes Ibn Abidin, who warns against giving fatwa solely from one late work, particularly unreliable ones like al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, etc., because their extreme brevity and textual errors led to misrepresenting the madhhab, sometimes attributing statements to the imams that they never held. The key takeaway: a mufti cannot simply pick any book; he must be aware of the scholarly consensus on its reliability.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the early Hanafi masters that are considered authoritative and foundational in the school.
غیر معتبر (ghayr mu'tabar): A book that is not considered reliable for issuing fatwas due to issues like unknown author, textual corruption, or lack of scholarly approval.
راجح (rajih): The preferred or stronger opinion in the madhhab, which is to be followed when giving fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin, why is giving fatwa solely from books like al-Durr al-Mukhtar and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir problematic?
A) They are too long and hard to reference.
B) They contain only weak (da'if) narrations.
C) Their extreme brevity and textual errors lead to misrepresenting the madhhab, sometimes attributing opinions to the imams that they never held.
D) They are only for Shafi'i fiqh.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must verify a book's scholarly standing and cross-reference multiple works to ensure the fatwa reflects the madhhab's relied-upon position.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Fifth Principle: Fatwa from Unreliable Books
Principle and conditions for using unreliable books in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a previously unreliable book becomes permissible for fatwa and apply the rule that removal of the illah reinstates reliability.

Core Idea
A book regains reliability for fatwa once the cause of its unreliability is eliminated.

Muftis often rely on trusted compendia, but sometimes they encounter a book previously declared unreliable. Does that mean it can never be used? The fifth principle of Rasm al-Mufti clarifies: if the reason for unreliability disappears, the book becomes usable. This lesson parses the scenarios and conditions set by later Hanafi authorities, equipping you to evaluate such cases in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its core mechanism
Read the opening sentence. The principle states that if a book is declared unreliable due to a cause (illah), and that cause later disappears, fatwa from it becomes permissible. The key is the removal of the illah.
illah is the reason for unreliability – e.g., rarity, unknown author, brevity.
2
List the four scenarios of illah removal
The passage gives four examples: (1) rarity cured by finding a corrected copy; (2) unknown author cured by discovering his scholarly standing; (3) extreme brevity cured by detailed discussion of a specific issue; (4) unknown source/origin cured by identifying the masdar and makhadh.
Each scenario involves a different cause; the remedy is specific to that cause.
3
Understand the role of supporting authorities
The quotes from Shaykh Salih al-Junaini and Allamah al-Lakhnawi add conditions. Junaini emphasizes knowing the source and origin; Lakhnawi says content must agree with reliable works, or else be abandoned.
These are not contradictions but additional checks: knowing the chain and content consistency.
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical case
Imagine a mufti finds a slim volume of Hanafi fatwas that was dismissed as unreliable because the author was unknown. Historical research proves the author was a respected student of Imam Abu Hanifa. Can he use it? Yes, because the illah (unknown author) is removed.
The principle applies to all four types; test each scenario mentally.

پانچواں اصول
غیر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا
جس کتاب کو کسی سبب اور علت کی بنیاد پر غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں وہ علت ختم ہو جائے تو پھر اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، مثلا جس کتاب کو اس کے نایاب ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں اس کا تصیح اور ثابت نسخہ مل جائے تو اب وہ کتاب معتبر ہو جائے گی اور اس سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا، اسی طرح جس کتاب کو اس کے مصنف کے احوال مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں اس مصنف کی علمی حالت سے لوگ آشنا ہو جائیں تو اب ان کی کتاب سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا ، اسی طرح جن کتابوں کو غیر معمولی اختصار کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور اسی کتاب میں کسی مسئلہ کی بابت خوب تفصیل موجود ہو تو صرف اس مسئلہ کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے وہ کتاب معتبر ہوگی، نیز غیر معتبر کتابوں کا مصدر وماخذ مل جائے تو اس سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا۔
شیخ صالح الجنینی فرماتے ہیں:
بر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب کہ اس کے مصدر ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اس کا علم ہو جائے اور اس کے ماخذ ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو اخذ کیا گیا ہے اس سے واقفیت ہو جائے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٥٦)
علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدائمی لکھنوی فرماتے ہیں: غیر معتبر کتابوں میں جو مسائل مذکور ہیں اگر وہ معتبر فقہی کتابوں کے موافق ہوں تو ان پر عمل کریں گے ورنہ انھیں ترک کر دیں گے، نیز ان مسائل کا اگر ما خذمل جائے تو ان پر عمل کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر وہ علت ختم ہو جائے جس کی وجہ سے وہ
Fifth Principle: Giving fatwa from unreliable books. A book that is declared unreliable due to a reason or cause, if that cause disappears, then there is no harm in giving fatwa from it. For example, a book declared unreliable due to its rarity, and later a corrected and confirmed copy is found—then that book becomes reliable and giving fatwa from it is permissible. Similarly, a book declared unreliable due to the unknown condition of its author, and later people become acquainted with the scholarly state of that author—then giving fatwa from his book is permissible. Similarly, books declared unreliable due to extreme brevity, but in that same book there is good detail about a particular issue—then only with reference to that issue the book is reliable. Also, if the source (masdar) and origin (makhadh) of the unreliable book are found, then giving fatwa from it is permissible. Shaykh Salih al-Junaini says: 'Giving fatwa from reliable books is permissible when its source (the book from which the issue is narrated) is known and its origin (the book from which the issue is derived) becomes known.' (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, p.56). Allamah Abu al-Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi says: 'Issues mentioned in unreliable books—if they agree with reliable fiqh books, we will act upon them; otherwise we will abandon them. Also, if the origin of these issues is found, there is no harm in acting upon them. Similarly, if the cause due to which they were [unreliable] disappears...'
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth principle: circumstances under which a book previously deemed unreliable may permissibly be used for fatwa. It lists several scenarios: (1) if the unreliability was due to the book being rare and a correct copy is later found; (2) if the author's scholarly standing was unknown and later becomes known; (3) if the unreliability was due to excessive brevity, but a particular issue is explained in detail therein—then that issue may be cited from that book; (4) if the source (masdar) and origin (makhadh) of the statements are identified—i.e., the original authorities from which the rulings are taken. Two later authorities are quoted: Shaykh Salih al-Junaini, who conditions permissibility on knowing the source and origin; and Allamah Lakhnawi, who adds that if the issues in an unreliable book agree with reliable works, they can be acted upon; otherwise, they are abandoned. The overarching principle: the cause (illah) that made the book unreliable must be removed.

Key Terms
علت (illah): The reason or cause for declaring a book unreliable, e.g., rarity, unknown author, brevity.
مصدر و ماخذ (masdar wa makhadh): Source and origin: respectively the book narrating the issue and the ultimate source from which it is derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fifth principle, for a book declared unreliable due to extreme brevity, when is it permissible to give fatwa from it?
A) Never, because brevity is permanent.
B) Only if a longer commentary exists.
C) If the book contains detailed discussion of that specific issue, it may be cited for that issue.
D) Only if the author writes a revised edition.

Key Takeaway
The unreliability of a book is not absolute; it is contingent on a cause that can be removed, restoring the book's usability for fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
