Fifth Principle: Causes of Book Unreliability (Causes 1-3)
Listing the general rule and first three causes for a book's unreliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three causes for a book's unreliability in the Hanafi school and apply the rule that removal of the cause restores reliability.

Core Idea
A book's unreliability is cause-based; when the cause ends, the book becomes reliable.

This lesson introduces the fifth principle of fatwa methodology: determining the reliability of books. The text explains that books may be declared unreliable due to specific causes, but once the cause is removed—whether it is rarity, unknown authorship, conciseness, or weak narrations—the book becomes usable. We will examine the first three causes in detail, with examples from Hanafi works.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the General Rule
Read the opening statement: if a cause for unreliability is removed, the book becomes reliable. Identify the three examples given: rarity resolved by finding a verified copy, unknown author resolved by learning of his status, extreme conciseness resolved by detailed discussion of a specific issue.
The rule is not permanent; reliability can be regained.
2
Analyze Cause 1: Unknown Author
Focus on the first cause: the author being unknown (majhūl) in identity or scholarly competence. Note the examples: Sharh al-Kanz by Ma Miskin, Jami' al-Rumuz by Quhistani, Khazanat al-Riwayat by Qadi Jakan. Understand why these are unreliable: the authors' scholarly status is not well-known.
This is analogous to hadith narration where the narrator's reliability must be known.
3
Analyze Cause 2: Weak Narrations
Examine the second cause: the book contains weak narrations without indication. Even if the author is known, if he collects all kinds of narrations without marking the weak ones, the book is unreliable. Examples: Qunyah al-Munyah by Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj by al-Haddad, al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah by al-Sufi.
The key point is that the weakness is not pointed out, misleading the mufti.
4
Analyze Cause 3: Extreme Conciseness
Study the third cause: expression being extremely concise. The text begins to explain that such books may be unreliable because their brevity obscures details. Note that if within such a book there is a detailed discussion of a particular issue, that part becomes reliable.
This cause is partially covered; the page cuts off, but the principle is clear: conciseness can cause unreliability unless detail is present.
5
Apply the Principle
Practice applying the rule: given a scenario where a book was declared unreliable due to rarity, but later a verified copy is found, determine that it becomes reliable. Similarly, if an author's competence becomes known, or if weak narrations are later identified and removed, the book's reliability is restored.
The mufti must continually reassess the causes.

غیر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا
شي عقود رسم المفر

بر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب کہ اس کے مصدر ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اس کا علم ہو جائے اور اس کے ماخذ ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو اخذ کیا گیا ہے اس سے واقفیت ہو جائے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٥٦)
علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدائمی لکھنوی فرماتے ہیں: غیر معتبر کتابوں میں جو مسائل مذکور ہیں اگر وہ معتبر فقہی کتابوں کے موافق ہوں تو ان پر عمل کریں گے ورنہ انھیں ترک کر دیں گے، نیز ان مسائل کا اگر ما خذمل جائے تو ان پر عمل کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر وہ علت ختم ہو جائے جس کی وجہ سے وہ
کتاب غیر معتبر ہوئی تھی تو اب وہ کتاب معتبر ہو جائے گی۔(عمدة الرعايه: ٦٣/١) کتابوں کے غیر معتبر ہونے کے دس (۱۰) اسباب
فقہ حنفی میں کسی کتاب کے غیر معتبر ہونے کے درج ذیل اسباب ہوتے ہیں: پہلا سبب : مؤلف کا مجہول ہونا
بعض کتابوں کو ان کے مصنفین کے اسماء کے مجہول ہونے اور ان کی علمی لیاقت کے غیر معروف ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ ما مسکین کی شرح الکنز ، علامہ قہستانی کی جامع الرموز فی شرح النقایہ اور قاضی جکن کی خزانة الروايات غیر معتبر کتابیں ہیں، کیوں کہ ان تینوں مصنفین کا علمی مقام مشہور و معروف نہیں ہے۔
حاشيه رسم المفتی : ٥٥ ، عمدة الرعايه : ٤٩ ، المذهب الحنفي: ٢٣٥/١)
:دوسرا سب کتاب کا ضعیف روایات پر مشتمل ہونا
بعض مصنفین ایسے ہیں جن کے علمی مراتب سے سبھی حضرات واقف ہیں، لیکن وہ اپنی کتابوں میں صحیح اقوال لکھنے کا التزام نہیں کرتے ہیں، بلکہ ہر طرح کی روایات واقوال کو جمع کر دیتے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دینے کے حق میں ان کی کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی ، چنانچہ علامہ زاہدی کی قنية المنيه ، علامہ ابوبکر بن على الحداد كي السراج الوهاج الموضح لكل طالب و محتاج اور علامہ فضل اللہ حمد بن ایوب صوفی کی الفتاوى الصوفيه غير معتبر کتابیں ہیں، کیوں کہ ان کتابوں میں بہت سے مقامات پر ضعیف اقوال نقل کئے گئے ہیں
اور ان کے ضعف کی جانب اشارہ بھی نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔
اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ۲۱۰ ، المصباح للراشدي : ٤٥٥ ، المذهب الحنفي: ۲۲۸/۱)
تیسرا سبب: عبارت کا انتہائی مختصر ہونا
بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن کی عبارتیں اس قدر مختصر ہیں کہ بسا اوقات مفتی کے لئے
The fifth principle: Giving fatwa from unreliable books. A book that has been declared unreliable on the basis of some cause and reason, and later that cause is removed, then there is no harm in giving fatwa from it. For example, a book declared unreliable because of its rarity, and later a corrected and verified copy is found, then that book becomes reliable and giving fatwa from it is permissible. Similarly, a book declared unreliable because of the unknown condition of its author, and later people become acquainted with the scholarly state of that author, then giving fatwa from his book becomes permissible. Similarly, books declared unreliable because of extreme conciseness, and in that same book there is detailed discussion regarding some issue, then that book becomes reliable only with respect to that issue. Also, if the source and origin of unreliable books are found, then giving fatwa from them is permissible. Shaykh Salih al-Junayni says: Giving fatwa from unreliable books is permissible when its source (i.e., the book from which the issue is narrated) becomes known and its origin (i.e., the book from which the issue is derived) becomes known. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 56) Allamah Abul-Hasanat Abdul-Hayy al-Lakhnawi says: Issues mentioned in unreliable books: if they agree with reliable fiqh books, we will act upon them; otherwise we will abandon them. Also, if the origin of those issues is found, there is no harm in acting upon them. Similarly, if the cause due to which the book became unreliable ceases, then that book becomes reliable. ('Umdat al-Ri'ayah: 1/63) The ten causes for books being unreliable: In the Hanafi fiqh, the following are the causes for a book being unreliable: The first cause: The author being unknown. Some books are declared unreliable because the names of their authors are unknown and their scholarly competence is unrecognized. For example, Sharh al-Kanz by Ma Miskin, Jami' al-Rumuz fi Sharh al-Nuqayah by Allamah Quhistani, and Khazanat al-Riwayat by Qadi Jakan are unreliable books, because the scholarly status of these three authors is not well-known. (Hashiyah Rasm al-Mufti: 55, 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah: 49, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/235) The second cause: The book containing weak narrations. Some authors are such that their scholarly ranks are known to all, but they do not commit to writing only correct statements in their books; rather they collect all kinds of narrations and sayings. Therefore, their books will be unreliable for the purpose of giving fatwa. For example, Qunyah al-Munyah by Allamah Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj al-Muwaddih li Kulli Talib wa Muhtaj by Allamah Abu Bakr ibn Ali al-Haddad, and al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah by Allamah Fadl Allah Hamad ibn Ayyub al-Sufi are unreliable books, because in these books weak sayings are transmitted in many places and their weakness is not indicated. (Usul al-Ifta' li al-Uthmani: 210, al-Misbah li al-Rashidi: 455, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/228) The third cause: The expression being extremely concise. Some books are such that their expressions are so concise that sometimes for the mufti...
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage addresses the fifth principle of giving fatwa from unreliable books. It first presents a general rule: if the cause for a book's unreliability is removed, it becomes reliable. Three examples follow: (1) rarity resolved by finding a verified copy, (2) unknown author resolved by learning of his scholarly status, (3) extreme conciseness resolved if there is detailed discussion of a specific issue, making the book reliable only for that issue. Additionally, if the source or origin of the content in an unreliable book becomes known, it becomes permissible to give fatwa from it. The author then quotes Shaykh Salih al-Junayni and Allamah Lakhnawi confirming this principle. Next, the passage begins to enumerate the ten causes for a book being unreliable within the Hanafi school. Only the first three causes are fully or partially given: (1) unknown author—exemplified by three specific books; (2) containing weak narrations—exemplified by three other books where weak statements are unmarked; (3) extremely concise expression—this cause is introduced but cut off at the end of the page. The passage relies on standard Hanafi juristic practice, not on direct scriptural proofs, and it is essential for a mufti to know which books are reliable and why. Note that a book declared unreliable due to one cause may still be used if that cause is removed or if its source is identified.

Key Terms
غیر معتبر کتاب (ghayr mu'tabar kitāb): A book that cannot be relied upon for issuing fatwas due to a recognized cause such as unknown author, weak narrations, or excessive conciseness.
مؤلف کا مجہول ہونا (mu'allif kā majhūl honā): The author being obscure or unknown in identity or scholarly competence, making the book unreliable.
ضعیف روایات (ḍaʻīf riwāyāt): Weak or unreliable transmissions (sayings or narrations) within a book, especially when not identified as weak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a cause for a book being considered unreliable?
A) The author being unknown.
B) The book containing weak narrations without indication.
C) The book being too lengthy.
D) The expression being extremely concise.

Key Takeaway
A book's reliability is not permanent; it depends on whether the cause for its unreliability has been removed.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
10 min
Five Causes of a Book Being Unreliable in Hanafi Ifta
Lists first five causes for book unreliability in fatwa methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and apply the first five causes that make a Hanafi fiqh book unreliable for issuing fatwas.

Core Idea
A book is reliable only when its author is known, its content is sound, its text is clear, and it is not declared weak.

In Hanafi usul al-ifta, not every fiqh book is acceptable as a source for fatwa. Later jurists established specific criteria to filter out unreliable works. This lesson presents the first five causes from Naseem Ul Mufti, which every mufti must know to avoid relying on weak materials. The causes range from the author's unknown status to the presence of weak narrations and ambiguous wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's standing
Check if the author's name and scholarly competence are known. If the author is majhul (unknown), the book is unreliable, regardless of content.
Example: Masakeen, Qahistani, and Qadi Jakan are considered unknown authors.
2
Assess the content's reliability
Examine whether the book contains weak narrations (da'if riwayat) without any indication. If it does, the book is unreliable even if the author is famous.
Example: Zahidi's Quniyat al-Munya contains weak statements without commentary.
3
Evaluate textual clarity
If the text is extremely concise and ambiguous, the book is unreliable until fully understood. Fatwa from such books is permissible only after complete comprehension.
Example: Al-Durr al-Mukhtar is concise; muftis must study it thoroughly before use.
4
Check for explicit declaration of weakness
If a reliable jurist (muhaqqiq) declares a book weak, it becomes unreliable, unless a higher-ranking jurist states otherwise.
Example: Mushtamil al-Ahkam was declared weak by al-Barkali and al-Lakhnawi.
5
Check the author's own status
If a jurist declares the author weak, all his books are unreliable, unless another higher-ranking jurist considers the author reliable.
Example: Ibn Abidin declared Zahidi weak because he transmits weak narrations.

تیسرا سبب: عبارت کا انتہائی مختصر ہونا
بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن کی عبارتیں اس قدر مختصر ہیں کہ بسا اوقات مفتی کے لئے ان عبارتوں کا سمجھنا انتہائی مشکل امر ہو جاتا ہے اور عبارات کے صحیح مفاہیم تک ان کی رسائی نہیں ہو پاتی ہے، لہذا ایسی کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی، چنانچہ علامہ عمربن نجیم کی النهر الفائق شرح كنز الدقائق ، علامہ بدرالدین عینی کی رمز الحقائق شرح کنز الدقائق اور علامہ حصلفى كى الدر المختار شرح تنویر الابصار غیر معتبر کتابیں ہیں، اس لیے کہ ان کتابوں کی عبارتیں انتہائی مختصر اور کافی پیچیدہ ہیں، لہذا ان کتابوں سے فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہو گا جب عبارت مکمل طور پر سمجھ میں آجائے اور کسی قسم کا خلجان باقی نہ رہے۔

جس کتاب کو کوئی محقق فقیہ یا کوئی بڑا عالم دین کسی سبب کی بنیاد پر ضعیف قرار دیں تو وہ کتاب بھی غیر معتبر ہوگی ، خواہ انھوں نے ہمارے سامنے کوئی سبب بیان کیا ہو یا نہیں ، الا یہ کہ اس کے خلاف دوسرے فقیہ کی صراحت موجود ہو اور وہ رتبہ میں ان سے بڑھے ہوئے ہوں تو پھر اس کتاب کو معتبر مانا جائے گا، چنانچہ علامہ فخر الدین یحیی بن عبد اللہ رومی کی مشتمل الأحكام فى الفتاوى الحنفيه غير معتبر کتاب ہے، اس لئے کہ علامہ محمد بن پیر علی برکلی اور علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدالحی لکھنوی نے اس کتاب کو ضعیف قرار دیا ہے۔
پانچواں سبب : مؤلف کا ضعیف ہوتا
(المذهب الحنفى : ۲۲۶/١)
جس مصنف کو کوئی فقیہ کسی سبب کی بنیاد پر ضعیف قراردیں تو ان کی تمام کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی لیکن اگر کسی دوسرے فقیہ نے ان کو معتبر مصنف قرار دیا ہو اور وہ دوسرا فقیہ علمی لحاظ سے پہلے سے بلند تر ہو تو پھر ان کی کتاب معتبر ہوگی ،مثلا علامہ زاہدی کے بارے میں علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں کہ زاہدی ضعیف روایات کو نقل کرتے ہیں، لہذا جس مسئلہ کو وہ تنہا بیان کریں اس میں ان کی اتباع نہیں کی جائے گی ، پس علامہ زاہدی کی قنیة
Ten (10) causes for a book being unreliable: In Hanafi fiqh, there are the following causes for a book being unreliable: First cause: The author being unknown (majhul). Some books are deemed unreliable due to their authors' names being unknown and their scholarly competence being unrecognized. For example, the following are unreliable: Sharh al-Kanz by Masakeen, Jami' al-Rumuz fi Sharh al-Nuqayah by Qahistani, and Khizanat al-Riwayat by Qadi Jakan, because the scholarly standing of these three authors is not well-known. (Hashiyah Rasm al-Mufti: 55, Umdat al-Riayah: 49, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/235). Second cause: The book consisting of weak narrations. Some authors are those whose scholarly rank is known to all, but they do not commit to writing sound statements; rather they collect all kinds of narrations and statements. Therefore, their books are unreliable for giving fatwa. For example, Quniyat al-Munya by Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj al-Mudhah li Kulli Talib wa Muhtaj by Abu Bakr bin Ali al-Haddad, and al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah by Fadlallah Hamid bin Ayyub al-Sufi are unreliable because in these books many places weak statements are transmitted and no indication of their weakness is given. (Usul al-Ifta' al-Uthmani: 210, al-Misbah li al-Rashidi: 455, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/228). Third cause: The text being extremely concise. Some books have texts so concise that often for the mufti understanding them becomes extremely difficult and they do not arrive at the correct meanings. Hence such books are unreliable. For example, al-Nahr al-Fa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Umar bin Nujaym, Ramz al-Haqa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Badr al-Din al-Ayni, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar Sharh Tanwir al-Absar by Hasafi are unreliable because their texts are extremely concise and quite complex. Therefore, giving fatwa from these books will be permissible only when the text is fully understood and no doubt remains. (Usul al-Ifta' al-Uthmani: 214, al-Misbah li al-Rashidi: 460, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/226). Fourth cause: The book being declared weak. A book that a verifying jurist or a great scholar declares weak for some reason is also unreliable, whether they mention the reason to us or not, unless there is an explicit statement from another jurist to the contrary and that jurist is higher in rank, then that book will be considered reliable. For example, Mushtamil al-Ahkam fi al-Fatawa al-Hanafiyyah by Fakhr al-Din Yahya bin Abdullah al-Rumi is unreliable because both Muhammad bin Pir Ali al-Barkali and Abu al-Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi declared it weak. Fifth cause: The author being declared weak. (al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/226). An author whom a jurist declares weak for some reason, then all his books will be unreliable. However, if another jurist considers him a reliable author and that second jurist is higher in scholarly standing than the first, then his book will be reliable. For example, regarding Zahidi, Ibn Abidin al-Shami says that Zahidi transmits weak narrations, so in a matter that he narrates alone, he is not to be followed. Thus, Zahidi's Qunyah... (text cuts off)
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a methodological enumeration of ten causes due to which a Hanafi fiqh book is considered unreliable for issuing fatwas. The text, from Naseem Ul Mufti, a commentary on Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, here presents the first five causes. The first cause is the author being unknown (majhul). If the author's identity or scholarly competence is not recognized, his book cannot be trusted. Examples include works by Masakeen, Qahistani, and Qadi Jakan. The second cause is that the book contains weak narrations without distinguishing them. Even if the author himself is known, if he collects all kinds of reports without indicating which are weak, the book is unreliable. Examples include Quniyat al-Munya by Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj by al-Haddad, and al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah by al-Sufi. The third cause is excessive brevity (ikhtisar mukhll). If the wording is so concise that it becomes difficult to understand correctly, the book is unreliable. Examples include al-Nahr al-Fa'iq, Ramz al-Haqa'iq, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. However, fatwa from such books is permissible if the mufti fully comprehends the text after study. The fourth cause is explicit declaration of weakness by a reliable jurist. If a muhaqqiq declares a book weak, it becomes unreliable unless a higher authority rules it reliable. The example given is Mushtamil al-Ahkam, declared weak by al-Barkali and al-Lakhnawi. The fifth cause is the author himself being declared weak. If a jurist declares the author unreliable, all his books become unreliable, unless a higher-ranking jurist regards the author as reliable. Ibn Abidin's criticism of Zahidi is cited: Zahidi alone is not followed because he transmits weak narrations. The passage thus establishes a hierarchy of authority for Hanafi fiqh books, ensuring that only reliable sources are used for ifta.

Key Terms
غیر معتبر (ghair mu'tabar): A book that is not accepted as a reliable source for issuing fatwas due to one or more of the listed causes.
مجہول (majhul): Unknown; referring to an author whose identity or scholarly standing is not known.
ضعیف روایات (da'if riwayat): Weak narrations or statements, often from unreliable sources, that are included in the book without comment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the five causes mentioned in the passage?
A) The author being unknown.
B) The book containing weak narrations.
C) The book being too long.
D) The text being extremely concise.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi fiqh book is reliable for fatwa only if the author is known, the content is free of weak narrations, the text is clear, and it has not been explicitly declared weak by a higher authority.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner

Sixth Cause: Doubt in Attribution of Books
Explains why doubt in authorship attribution renders a book unreliable for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a book's attribution is doubtful and apply the rule that such a book is unreliable for fatwa.

Core Idea
A book's authority depends on sound attribution — doubt in authorship renders it unreliable for fatwa.

In this lesson, we examine the sixth cause that makes a book unreliable: doubt in its attribution to its author. Even if a scholar is well-known, a book attributed to them must have a proven chain of transmission. We look at two classical examples to understand how this principle is applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the attributed author and the book
Determine the author to whom the book is ascribed and the title of the book.
2
Check the chain of attribution
Investigate whether the book's attribution to that author is established through a sound chain (sahih sanad) by checking standard Hanafi bibliographical sources.
If there is doubt (shakk) — e.g., other scholars attribute it to someone else, or it was compiled posthumously by an unknown person — then the chain is not sound.
3
Apply the rule to the examples
For al-Makhārij fī al-Ḥiyal, note that its attribution to Imam Abu Yusuf is not correct, and it has been published under the name of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. For al-Fatāwā al-ʿAzīziyya, note that it was compiled after Shah Abdul Aziz's death by an unknown person who added unverified fatawa.
4
Conclude on the book's reliability
Since the attribution is doubtful, the book is considered ghayr mu'tabar (unreliable) for fatwa. It should not be used as a source for issuing rulings.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھٹا سبب : کتاب کی نسبت میں شک ہونا
بعض کتابوں کو اس لئے غیر معتبر قرار دیا گیا ہے کہ جن مصنفین کی طرف وہ کتابیں منسوب ہیں ان کی طرف ان کتابوں کی نسبت میں شک ہے اور ان کتابوں کا انھیں مصنفین کی کتابیں ہونا صحیح سند سے ثابت نہیں ہے، مثلا المخارج فی الحیل غیر معتبر کتاب ہے کیوں کہ یہ کتاب گرچہ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کی طرف منسوب ہے لیکن یہ نسبت صحیح نہیں ہے، جیسا کہ المذهب الحنفی میں اس کی صراحت کی گئی ہے، نیز مکتبہ قاہرہ سے یہی کتاب امام محمد بن حسن شیبانی کے نام سے شائع ہوئی ہے، اسی طرح شاہ عبدالعزیز محدث دہلوی کی طرف منسوب الفتاوی العزیزیہ بھی غیر معتبر کتاب ہے، اس لئے کہ شیخ الاسلام مفتی تقی عثمانی صاحب کے بقول یہ آپ کی تالیف نہیں ہے، بلکہ آپ کی وفات کے بعد ایک غیر معروف آدمی نے آپ کے فتاوی کو جمع کر دیا ہے اور اس نے اس کتاب میں ان فتاوی کا بھی اضافہ کر دیا ہے جو حضرت دہلوی سے منقول نہیں ہیں۔
(المذهب الحنفى : ۲۳۹/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ٢١٦)
Sixth cause: Doubt in attribution of a book. Some books have been deemed unreliable because there is doubt in their attribution to the authors to whom they are ascribed, and it is not proven by sound chain that these books are actually by those authors. For example, al-Makharij fi'l-Hiyal is an unreliable book because although it is attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, this attribution is not correct, as clarified in al-Madhhab al-Hanafi. Moreover, from the Qahirah Library, this same book was published under the name of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. Similarly, al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya attributed to Shah Abdul Aziz Muhaddith Dehlawi is also an unreliable book because, according to Shaykh al-Islam Mufti Taqi Uthmani, it is not his composition; rather, after his death, an unknown person collected his fatawa and added to this book fatawa that are not transmitted from Shah Abdul Aziz.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage lists the sixth cause that renders a book unreliable for fatwa: doubt in the authorship attribution of the book. The author gives two examples: (1) al-Makharij fi'l-Hiyal, often attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, but this attribution is incorrect; even the book has been published under the name of Imam Muhammad instead. (2) al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya attributed to Shah Abdul Aziz Dehlawi, but according to Mufti Taqi Uthmani, it was compiled after his death by an unknown person who added material not from Shah Abdul Aziz. The principle is that for a book to be a reliable source for fatwa, its chain of attribution to its author must be sound and well-established. Doubt in attribution undermines the book's authority, even if the author is a great scholar. This rule prevents the spread of incorrect or fabricated rulings attributed to early authorities.

Key Terms
المخارج فی الحیل (al-Makhārij fī al-Ḥiyal): A book attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf but of doubtful attribution, thus deemed unreliable.
الفتاوی العزیزیۃ (al-Fatāwā al-ʿAzīziyya): A collection of fatawa attributed to Shah Abdul Aziz Dehlawi but compiled after his death by an unknown person with additions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is al-Makharij fi'l-Hiyal considered unreliable?
A) Its author was unknown.
B) Its attribution to Imam Abu Yusuf is not correct and has been published under another name.
C) It contains rulings contradictory to the majority.
D) It is a rare book not widely available.

Key Takeaway
A book is unreliable for fatwa if its attribution to its claimed author is doubtful, even if the author is a great scholar.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Seventh Cause: Books of Other Disciplines Are Not Sources for Fatwa
Explains the rasm rule that books of other disciplines are not reliable sources for fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify non-fiqh books that are unreliable for fatwa and apply the rule that incidental mention is insufficient.

Core Idea
Fatwa must be based on primary fiqh works, not on incidental mentions in hadith commentaries or other disciplines.

In the Hanafi tradition, a mufti must rely on dedicated fiqh works to ensure accuracy. This lesson explains why books from other disciplines—like hadith commentaries, usul al-fiqh, or theology—are not reliable for fatwa, even if they contain fiqh rulings. Understanding this principle protects against error by ensuring that every fatwa is grounded in authoritative, systematic fiqh sources.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the core principle: a book belonging to a discipline other than fiqh is not a reliable source for fatwa because any fiqh issues it mentions are incidental.
This is one of the causes listed in Rasm al-Mufti works.
2
Identify the scope
Which types of books fall under this rule? The author mentions hadith commentaries, usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and other disciplines where fiqh appears collaterally.
Primary fiqh works (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Mabsut) are excluded from this ruling.
3
List the examples
Memorize the three examples given: 'Umdat al-Qari (commentary on Bukhari), Mirqat al-Mafatih (commentary on Mishkat), and Mubariq al-Azhar (commentary on Mashariq).
These are excellent works in their fields, but their primary subject is not fiqh.
4
Note the exception
If the same fiqh issue is also transmitted in a proper fiqh work, then it is permissible to give fatwa from the non-fiqh book as a reference, but the primary reliance should still be the fiqh source.
This exception prevents unnecessary restriction when the ruling is well-attested.
5
Apply the rule
Given a book, determine its primary discipline. If it is not a dedicated fiqh work, its use for fatwa is restricted unless the ruling is corroborated by a fiqh source.
Practice identifying primary vs. non-primary fiqh books.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتواں سبب کتاب کا فقہ کے علاوہ دیگر فنون میں ہونا
جن کتابوں میں فقہی مسائل کو ضمنی طور پر ذکر کیا جاتا ہے، جیسے اصول تغیر ، شروح حدیث، اصول فقہ اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر فنون کی کتابوں میں کسی اصول کی وضاحت کرتے وقت فقہی مسائل کا تذکرہ ضمنا آجاتا ہے، تو اس مسئلہ کی بابت اس کتاب سے فتوی دینے کی حیثیت سے وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہوگی، چنانچہ علامہ بدرالدین معینی کی عمدۃ القاری شرح بخاری اور مرقاۃ المفاتیح شرح مشکوۃ المصابیح، نیز علامہ عبداللطیف بن عبدالعزیز بن ملک کی مبارق الازھار شرح مشارق الانوار سے فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ ان کتابوں میں فقہی مسائل کا تذکرہ ضمنا اور تبعا آیا ہے، البتہ اگر وہ مسئلہ فقہی کتابوں میں بھی اسی طرح منقول ہو تو پھر اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
(المذهب الحنفي: ۲۳۰/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ۲۱۷)
Seventh cause: The book belonging to disciplines other than fiqh. Books in which fiqh issues are mentioned incidentally, such as books of usul al-din, hadith commentaries, usul al-fiqh, and other disciplines where fiqh issues are mentioned collaterally while explaining some principle, then with respect to that issue, such a book is unreliable for giving fatwa. Therefore, it is not permissible to give fatwa from 'Umdat al-Qari (commentary on Bukhari), Mirqat al-Mafatih (commentary on Mishkat al-Masabih), and Mubariq al-Azhar (commentary on Mashariq al-Anwar) because in these books fiqh issues are mentioned incidentally and secondarily. However, if that same issue is also transmitted in fiqh books, then there is no harm in giving fatwa from them.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage lists the seventh cause that renders a book unreliable for fatwa: it belongs to a discipline other than fiqh. The principle is that fatwa should be derived from dedicated fiqh works, not from commentaries on hadith, usul, or theology, where fiqh rulings appear only incidentally. The author gives three examples: 'Umdat al-Qari (a commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari by Badr al-Din al-Ayni), Mirqat al-Mafatih (a commentary on Mishkat al-Masabih by Mulla Ali al-Qari), and Mubariq al-Azhar (a commentary on Mashariq al-Anwar by Abd al-Latif ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Malik). These are excellent works in their fields, but because fiqh is not their primary subject, their mention of fiqh is merely incidental and cannot be relied upon for fatwa unless the same ruling is found in a proper fiqh source. This ensures that fatwas are based on authoritative, systematic fiqh works rather than secondary references.

Key Terms
عمدة القاري (ʿUmdat al-Qārī): A famous commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari by Badr al-Din al-Ayni; mentioned as an example of a non-fiqh book not to be used for fatwa.
مرقاة المفاتیح (Mirqāt al-Mafātīḥ): Commentary on Mishkat al-Masabih by Mulla Ali al-Qari; another example of a book not to be used for fatwa.
مبارق الأزهار (Mubāriq al-Azhār): Commentary on Mashariq al-Anwar by Abd al-Latif ibn Abd al-Aziz; third example of a non-fiqh book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following books is not to be used for fatwa because it is not a primary fiqh work?
A) al-Hidayah
B) 'Umdat al-Qari
C) al-Mabsut
D) al-Jami' al-Saghir

Key Takeaway
Fatwa must be based on dedicated fiqh works, not on incidental mentions in books of other disciplines, unless the ruling is corroborated by a fiqh source.

Eighth Cause: Rarity of a Book
Explains why a rare book cannot be used for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a rare or unavailable book cannot be used as a source for fatwa until it is verified and accessible.

Core Idea
A fatwa must be based on accessible, verified texts; a rare book is unreliable until it becomes available.

In the previous lessons, we learned that a mufti must rely on authoritative sources within the Hanafi school. However, not every book that appears in early references is automatically usable. This lesson explains the eighth cause from the Rasm al-Mufti: the rarity of a book. Even a famous work like al-Muhit al-Burhani was initially prohibited for fatwa because no copies were available. We will see how availability and verification determine a book's legal usability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Recognize that a book cannot be used for fatwa if it is rare and its text is not accessible. This is a standing rule in Hanafi iftaa.
2
Understand the Basis
The requirement of a sound chain (sanad) for the book: without a reliable copy, the text cannot be verified.
This parallels the requirement for hadith transmission.
3
Recognize the Exception
If a verified printed or manuscript copy becomes available with a sound chain, the book becomes permissible for fatwa.
The status can change over time.
4
Apply to the Example
Al-Muhit al-Burhani was forbidden until it was published with scholarly research and verification.
Now it is a reliable source.
5
Extract the Principle
The mufti must stay updated on the availability of works; a source's usability is dynamic.
Consult contemporary scholars on new editions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آٹھواں سبب کتاب کا نایاب ہونا
بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن کا نام متقدمین کی کتابوں میں ملتا ہے لیکن ان کا مطبوعہ یا مخطوطہ نسخہ اب دستیاب نہیں ہے، لہذا مخطوطات پر تحقیقی نظر رکھنے والا کوئی عالم اگر کسی کتاب کو نایاب قرار دے تو پھر اس کتاب سے فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہوگا، مگر یہ کہ اس کا مطبوعہ یا مخطوطہ نسخہ صحیح سند سے دستیاب ہو جائے، مثلا بعض فقہاء نے المحیط البرهاني في الفقه النعمانی سے فتوی دینے سے منع کیا تھا، اس لئے کہ اس وقت اس کا مخطوطہ یا مطبوعہ نسخہ دستیاب نہیں تھا، جیسا کہ علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدالحی لکھنوی نے اس کی صراحت کی ہے لیکن اب یہ کتاب شیخ الاسلام مفتی تقی عثمانی کے بھانجے مولانا نعیم اشرف نور احمد عثمانی کی تحقیق کے ساتھ ادارۃ القرآن و العلوم الاسلامیہ کراچی پاکستان سے ۲۵ جلدوں میں شائع ہو چکی ہے، اس لئے اب اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
(المذهب الحنفى: ۲۳۲/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: (٢١٥)
Eighth cause: Rarity of a book. Some books are such that their name is found in the books of early scholars, but their printed or manuscript copy is now unavailable. Therefore, if a scholar who has a research eye on manuscripts declares a book to be rare, then it is not permissible to give fatwa from that book, unless its printed or manuscript copy becomes available with a sound chain. For example, some jurists forbade giving fatwa from al-Muhit al-Burhani fi al-Fiqh al-Nu'mani because at that time its manuscript or printed copy was not available, as clarified by Allamah Abu al-Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi. But now this book has been published in 25 volumes from Idarat al-Quran wa al-Ulum al-Islamiyyah, Karachi, Pakistan, under the research of Maulana Naeem Ashraf Noor Ahmad Uthmani, the nephew of Shaykh al-Islam Mufti Taqi Uthmani, so now there is no harm in giving fatwa from it.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage lists the eighth cause: a book is unreliable for fatwa if it is rare and its copies are not available. The reasoning is that without access to the actual text, one cannot verify the content or chain. The example given is al-Muhit al-Burhani, a major Hanafi fiqh work. Early scholars (like Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi) forbade using it because no copies were available. However, once it was published with scholarly verification, it became permissible to use it. This shows that the status of a book can change over time based on availability and verification. The rule emphasizes that fatwa must be based on accessible, verifiable sources, not on references to lost or rare works.

Key Terms
المحيط البرهاني (al-Muḥīṭ al-Burhānī): A Hanafi fiqh work that was initially rare and thus not used for fatwa until it was published with research.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why was al-Muhit al-Burhani initially not a source for fatwa?
A) It was written by a non-Hanafi scholar.
B) It contained many printing errors.
C) Its manuscript or printed copy was not available at that time.
D) It was attributed to the wrong author.

Key Takeaway
A book's usability for fatwa depends on its availability and verified transmission; even a famous work cannot be used if it is rare.

The Requirement of Accurate Texts: The Ninth Cause of Unreliability
Begins explaining why books with many printing errors are unreliable for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why printing errors make a book unreliable for fatwa and apply the principle of verification when selecting sources.

Core Idea
A book with extensive printing errors is unreliable for fatwa; the mufti must verify accuracy.

This lesson addresses a modern challenge: the proliferation of printing errors in computer-typed books. The ninth cause in 'Naseem al-Mufti' explains that errors persist across editions because typists are often not scholars. As a mufti, you must ensure the texts you rely on are free from significant errors, or your fatwa may be incorrect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognize that extensive printing errors constitute a distinct cause of unreliability for fatwa sources. The author lists it as the ninth cause.
This is a rasm al-mufti principle: the condition of the physical text matters.
2
Recognize the modern context
Understand that computer typing by non-scholars leads to many errors. These errors are then transmitted to subsequent editions.
The problem is compounded when editors do not consult the original manuscript.
3
Apply the principle
As a mufti, you must avoid relying on books known for pervasive errors unless you have access to a corrected edition or have personally verified the text.
This may involve checking multiple editions, comparing with reliable copies, or consulting experts.
4
Consider implications
An erroneous text can lead to a incorrect fatwa, which is a serious matter in Islamic law. The mufti bears responsibility for the accuracy of his sources.
The principle aligns with the broader requirement of 'tahqiq al-masail' (verification of issues).

Therefore, many printing errors remain in books, and those errors keep transferring from one edition to another. The author...

This passage introduces the ninth cause: extensive printing errors make a book unreliable for fatwa. The author notes that in modern times, with computer typing, many errors occur because typists are usually not scholars, and errors persist across editions. The text is incomplete, but the principle is clear: a book with numerous errors cannot be trusted for fatwa unless it is carefully checked and corrected. This rule ensures that fatwas are based on accurate texts. The passage ends abruptly; additional content likely follows on subsequent pages.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Eighth Cause: Book Becoming Rare (Nayab)
Explains that a rare book cannot be used for fatwa unless a reliable copy is found.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a rare book cannot be used for fatwa until a reliable copy is found, and identify the exception when such a copy becomes available.

Core Idea
A rare book is unusable for fatwa until a verified copy emerges.

A mufti's authority rests on reliable sources. When a book becomes rare—meaning no trustworthy printed or manuscript copy exists—it cannot be cited for fatwa. This lesson explains the ruling, its exception, and a historical example from Hanafi practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
A book is considered rare (nayab) when no reliable printed or manuscript copy is available. A qualified scholar with manuscript expertise declares it so.
2
Apply the default ruling
Once a book is declared rare, it is not permissible (ja'iz) to give fatwa from it, because the text cannot be verified.
This ruling is found in later Hanafi usul works.
3
Recognize the exception
If a reliable copy—either printed or manuscript with a sound chain (sahih sanad)—becomes available, the prohibition is lifted and fatwa becomes permissible again.
4
Analyze the historical example
Al-Muhit al-Burhani was once unavailable, so scholars forbade its use. Later, a critical edition was published, restoring its permissibility.
This demonstrates that the ruling is contingent on availability, not permanence.
5
Derive the underlying principle
The permissibility of using a book for fatwa depends on access to a verified copy. Without verification, the source lacks authority.
This principle is a subset of 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'—intentions require reliable means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آٹھواں سبب کتاب کا نایاب ہونا بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن کا نام متقدمین کی کتابوں میں ملتا ہے لیکن ان کا مطبوعہ یا مخطوطہ نسخہ اب دستیاب نہیں ہے، لہذا مخطوطات پر تحقیقی نظر رکھنے والا کوئی عالم اگر کسی کتاب کو نایاب قرار دے تو پھر اس کتاب سے فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہوگا، مگر یہ کہ اس کا مطبوعہ یا مخطوطہ نسخہ صحیح سند سے دستیاب ہو جائے، مثلا بعض فقہاء نے المحیط البرهاني في الفقه النعمانی سے فتوی دینے سے منع کیا تھا، اس لئے کہ اس وقت اس کا مخطوطہ یا مطبوعہ نسخہ دستیاب نہیں تھا، جیسا کہ علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدالحی لکھنوی نے اس کی صراحت کی ہے لیکن اب یہ کتاب شیخ الاسلام مفتی تقی عثمانی کے بھانجے مولانا نعیم اشرف نور احمد عثمانی کی تحقیق کے ساتھ ادارۃ القرآن و العلوم الاسلامیہ کراچی پاکستان سے ۲۵ جلدوں میں شائع ہو چکی ہے، اس لئے اب اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ المذهب الحنفى: ۲۳۲/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: (٢١٥)
Eighth cause: The book becoming rare. Some books are mentioned in the works of the early scholars, but their printed or manuscript copy is now unavailable. Therefore, if a scholar who has research insight into manuscripts declares a book to be rare, then it is not permissible to give fatwa from that book, unless its printed or manuscript copy becomes available with a sound chain. For example, some jurists forbade giving fatwa from Al-Muhit al-Burhani fi al-Fiqh al-Nu'mani, because at that time its manuscript or printed copy was not available, as Allamah Abu al-Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi has clarified. But now this book has been published in 25 volumes with the research of Maulana Naeem Ashraf Noor Ahmad Uthmani, the nephew of Shaykh al-Islam Mufti Taqi Uthmani, from Idarat al-Quran wa al-Ulum al-Islamiyyah, Karachi, Pakistan. Therefore, there is no harm now in giving fatwa from it. Al-Madhhab al-Hanafi 1/232, Usool al-Ifta lil-Uthmani (215).
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth cause that affects the reliability of a book for issuing fatwas: the book becoming rare (nayab). The rule is that if a book is no longer available in either printed or manuscript form, and a qualified scholar declares it rare, then that book cannot be used as a source for fatwa. However, once a reliable copy—with a sound chain of transmission—becomes available, it becomes permissible again. The passage provides a concrete historical example: Al-Muhit al-Burhani, a Hanafi fiqh work, was previously unavailable, so scholars forbade using it. Later, when it was edited and published by a reliable scholar, the prohibition was lifted. This illustrates that the ruling is not permanent but contingent on availability. The references to Al-Madhhab al-Hanafi and Usool al-Ifta indicate the source of this rule in Hanafi usul literature.

Key Terms
نایاب (nayab): A book that is no longer available in any reliable printed or manuscript form.
مخطوطہ (makhṭūṭah): A handwritten manuscript of a book.
صحیح سند (ṣaḥīḥ sanad): A sound chain of transmission verifying the copy's authenticity from the author.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did some Hanafi jurists initially forbid giving fatwa from Al-Muhit al-Burhani?
A) Because the book contained errors in fiqh rulings
B) Because the book was not written by a Hanafi scholar
C) Because the book was not available in any reliable copy at that time
D) Because the book contradicted the Qur'an and Sunnah

Key Takeaway
A rare book cannot be used for fatwa until a reliable copy is verified; availability determines permissibility.

The Ninth Cause: Many Printing Errors
Expands on a rasm al-mufti rule about printing errors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a book with many printing errors is unreliable for fatwa until a verified corrected edition is available.

Core Idea
A book with many printing errors is unreliable for fatwa until a corrected edition emerges.

In the digital age, books are often typed by non-specialists, introducing errors that persist across editions. Muftis must verify the textual accuracy of their sources. This lesson teaches you how to identify when printing errors render a book unfit for issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognize that 'many printing errors' is a distinct cause of unreliability. The passage specifies that these errors are often the result of non-scholar typists and profit-driven publishers.
2
Understand the context
Appreciate the modern context: computer typing by non-scholars leads to errors that transfer between editions. The author's corrections are ignored by publishers.
This is a practical issue in contemporary fatwa work.
3
Apply the rule
If a book has many printing errors, it is 'ghayr mu'tabar' (unreliable). A mufti should not rely on it until a corrected edition is found.
Minor typos alone may not disqualify a book.
4
Note the condition for reliability
The book becomes reliable again only when a correct edition is located. This requires verification against the author's intended text.
A single corrected edition suffices.
5
Consider the mufti's responsibility
A mufti must actively ensure the reliability of his sources. Using an error-ridden book risks issuing incorrect fatwas.
This is part of the adab al-mufti (mufti's conduct).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نواں سبب طباعت میں کثیر اغلاط کا ہونا عصر حاضر میں کمپیوٹر کتابت کا رواج بہت بڑھ گیا ہے اور ٹائپنگ کرنے والے افراد عموما عالم یا محقق نہیں ہوتے ہیں، اس لئے کتابوں میں طباعت کی بہت سی اغلاط باقی رہ جاتی ہیں اور وہ غلطیاں ایک ایڈیشن سے دوسرے ایڈیشن میں منتقل ہوتی رہتی ہیں، مصنف کی ہزار خواہش اور تنبیہ کے باوجود کتب خانہ والے اپنے مفاد کے پیش نظر پہلا نسخہ ہی شائع کرتے رہتے ہیں، اس لئے اگر کسی کتاب میں طباعت کی بہت سی غلطیاں موجود ہوں تو وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہوگی جب تک کہ اس کا دوسرا صحیح نسخہ نہ مل جائے۔
Ninth cause: The presence of many printing errors in the publication. In the present age, the practice of computer typing has greatly increased, and the people doing the typing are generally not scholars or researchers. Therefore, many printing errors remain in books, and those errors keep transferring from one edition to another. Despite the author's thousands of wishes and warnings, the publishers, for their own benefit, keep publishing the first version. Therefore, if a book has many printing errors, that book will be unreliable until another correct edition is found.

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth cause that makes a book unreliable for fatwa: the existence of numerous printing errors. The contemporary context is computer typing by non-scholars, leading to errors that persist across editions. Publishers often reprint the same flawed edition for profit, ignoring the author's corrections. The rule is that such a book is not considered reliable (ghayr mu'tabar) until a corrected edition becomes available. This is a practical consideration for muftis: they must verify the textual accuracy of the books they use. The passage emphasizes that error-ridden books cannot be trusted for issuing fatwas, as even a single mistake could lead to an incorrect ruling.

Key Terms
اغلاط طباعت (aghlāṭ ṭibā‘ah): Printing errors, mistakes in the typesetting or transcription of a book.
غیر معتبر (ghayr mu‘tabar): Not reliable or authoritative for use in issuing fatwas.

Tenth Cause: Unclear Handwriting and Fatwa Reliability
Rule: manuscript readability condition for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a manuscript with unclear handwriting is unreliable for fatwa and apply the condition of certainty of reading to permit its use.

Core Idea
A manuscript is unreliable for fatwa unless its text can be read with certainty.

A mufti must rely on texts whose content he can accurately decipher. This lesson addresses a practical challenge: manuscripts with unclear handwriting, especially after digitization. You will learn when such books may still be used and the threshold of certainty required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognise that unclear handwriting (kitābah) is a distinct cause that renders a manuscript unreliable for fatwa.
The author lists this as the tenth cause, indicating a systematic approach to evaluating sources.
2
Assess readability
Evaluate whether the handwriting is so unclear that reading the correct text becomes extremely difficult, especially after scanning or uploading as PDF.
Personal experience of the author highlights that even a page or two may be impossible to read.
3
Determine default reliability
Conclude that such books are generally unreliable (ghayr mu‘tabar) for fatwa due to the risk of misreading.
This is the default ruling: if the text cannot be read with ease, do not use it.
4
Apply the exception of certainty
If after effort the correct reading of the text is verified with certainty (yaqīn), then the manuscript becomes permissible to use for fatwa.
Certainty here means overcoming the difficulty and being sure of the wording.

Tenth cause: The handwriting being unclear. Al-Madhhab al-Hanafi 1/233-234. Some manuscripts are such that their handwriting is not clear and readable, and reading the correct text is extremely difficult. Especially when PDF files of such manuscripts are made and uploaded on the internet, then their readability becomes even more difficult and complicated. The author himself has many such manuscripts on his mobile phone whose handwriting is so unclear that reading even a page or two is difficult. Therefore, such books will be unreliable for the purpose of giving fatwa, but when certainty about the correct reading of the text is achieved, then there is no harm in giving fatwa. Al-Madhhab al-Hanafi 1/234.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents the tenth cause that renders a book unreliable for fatwa: unclear handwriting of the manuscript. The rule is that if a manuscript's script is illegible or extremely difficult to read, especially when digitized into PDFs and uploaded online where readability may worsen, then such books cannot be trusted for issuing fatwas. However, once the correct reading of the text is verified with certainty, it becomes permissible. The author mentions his own experience with such manuscripts. This is a practical guideline for muftis: they must not rely on texts they cannot read accurately, as any misreading could lead to an incorrect fatwa. The references to Al-Madhhab al-Hanafi indicate the authority of this rule.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitābah): The handwriting or script of a manuscript.
خواندگی (khwāndagī): Readability, the ability to decipher the text.

The Hierarchy of Hanafi Rulings: Zahir al-Riwayah
Explaining the necessity of knowing the hierarchical classes of Hanafi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three classes of Hanafi rulings and state the definition, sources, and authority of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the bedrock of Hanafi fatwa—rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books carry the highest authority.

A mufti cannot issue sound fatwas without understanding the hierarchy of Hanafi rulings. This lesson introduces the three classes—Zahir al-Riwayah, Ghayr Zahir al-Riwayah, and Fatawa—and explains why Zahir al-Riwayah is the most authoritative. Knowing this hierarchy ensures that fatwas are based on the strongest evidence within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three classes
According to the passage, Hanafi rulings are divided into three classes: Zahir al-Riwayah (well-known transmitted rulings), Ghayr Zahir al-Riwayah (less well-known), and Fatawa (later fatwas). These have different levels of strength.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the strongest.
2
Define Zahir al-Riwayah
Zahir al-Riwayah refers to rulings transmitted from the three main imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) in the six books of Imam Muhammad via well-known, trustworthy chains.
The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' itself indicates 'well-known transmission'.
3
List the six books
The six books are: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir.
Memorize this list—it is foundational for identifying Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Identify the transmitters (as'hab al-madhhab)
For Zahir al-Riwayah, the 'founders of the school' are specifically the three imams (ulama' thalatha): Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Sometimes others are included, but the predominant view limits it to these three.
This precision avoids confusion when determining authenticity.
5
Understand the authority of Zahir al-Riwayah
Because of reliable transmission, Zahir al-Riwayah rulings take precedence over other classes when issuing fatwas. A mufti must prefer them when available.
This is a key rule in the mufti's methodology (rasm al-mufti).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتواں اصول مفتی کا مسائل احناف کے طبقات سے واقف ہونا فقہ حنفی کے بعض مسائل پر ظاہر الروایہ بعض مسائل پر غیر ظاہر الروایہ اور بعض مسائل پر فتاوی کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے اور یہ تینوں مسائل قوت کے اعتبار سے ایک دوسرے سے بڑھے ہوئے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دیتے وقت اس بات کا لحاظ رکھنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ جس قول پر وہ فتوی دے رہا ہے فقہ حنفی میں اس کا مقام و مرتبہ کیا ہے اور طبقات میں اس کی سندی حیثیت کیا ہے۔ مسائل احناف کے تین طبقات مشہور قول کے مطابق فقہ حنفی کے مسائل کے تین طبقات ہیں جو درج ذیل ہیں: پہلا طبقہ: ظاہر الروایہ مسائل کے پہلے طبقہ پر ظاہر الروایہ ، مسائل الاصول اور رولیۃ الاصول کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے اور اس طبقہ میں ان مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جو امام محمد کی چھ کتابوں یعنی مبسوط، جامع صغیر، جامع کبیر، زیادات، سیر صغیر اور سیر کبیر میں اصحاب مذہب سے منقول ہیں، چوں کہ یہ مسائل امام محمد سے مشہور و معروف طریقہ سے منقول ہیں اور ان مسائل کو نقل کرنے والے معتبر اور ثقہ افراد ہیں، اس لئے ان مسائل کو ظاہر الروایہ کہا جاتا ہے اور اسی لئے ان کی استنادی حیثیت دوسرے مسائل کی بہ نسبت زیادہ ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ اصحاب مذہب سے مراد احناف کے علماء ثلاثہ یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد ہیں، بسا اوقات اصحاب مذہب میں ان کے ساتھ امام زفر حسن بن زیاد اور ان کے علاوہ ان فقہاء کو بھی شامل کر لیا جاتا ہے جنھوں نے امام ابوحنیفہ سے علم فقہ حاصل کیا ہے، لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کے سلسلہ میں غالب اور مروج بات یہی ہے کہ وہ یا تو علماء ثلاثہ کا متفق علیہ قول ہوتا ہے یا ان میں سے کسی ایک کا قول ہوتا ہے۔
Seventh Principle: The mufti's familiarity with the classes of Hanafi rulings. Some Hanafi rulings are classified as Zahir al-Riwayah, some as Ghayr Zahir al-Riwayah, and some as Fatawa. These three types have different levels of strength. Therefore, when issuing a fatwa, it is necessary to consider the rank and evidentiary status of the statement in the Hanafi school. According to the well-known view, the rulings of the Hanafi school have three classes, as follows: First class: Zahir al-Riwayah. The first class is called Zahir al-Riwayah, Masail al-Usul, and Riwayat al-Usul. This class includes those rulings that are transmitted from the founders of the school in the six books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. Since these rulings are transmitted from Imam Muhammad in a well-known manner and the transmitters are trustworthy, they are called Zahir al-Riwayah, and their authority is greater than that of other rulings. It is clear that by 'founders of the school' are meant the three scholars: Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad. Sometimes Imam Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and other jurists who acquired fiqh from Imam Abu Hanifa are also included. But regarding Zahir al-Riwayah, the predominant view is that it is either an agreed-upon statement of the three scholars or a statement of one of them.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage introduces the seventh principle of mufti conduct: knowledge of the tabaqat (classes) of Hanafi rulings. It explains that rulings are divided into three levels: Zahir al-Riwayah (well-known transmitted rulings), Ghayr Zahir al-Riwayah (less well-known), and Fatawa (later fatwas). Each level has different weight, and a mufti must know the status of the ruling he is using. The first and strongest class is Zahir al-Riwayah, which comes from Imam Muhammad's six core books. These are considered the most authoritative because they are transmitted through reliable chains from the three main imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage clarifies that while the term 'as'hab al-madhhab' sometimes includes other students of Abu Hanifa, for Zahir al-Riwayah it refers specifically to these three or one of them.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The class of rulings transmitted in the six books of Imam Muhammad from the founders of the Hanafi school.
اصحاب مذہب (as'hab al-madhhab): Primarily refers to the three main imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
علماء ثلاثہ (ulama' thalatha): The three scholars: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat
C) Al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Ashbah, al-Nazair
D) Al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah from Imam Muhammad's six books is the most authoritative class of Hanafi rulings; a mufti must know and apply this hierarchy when issuing fatwas.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Layers of Hanafi Rulings for the Mufti: Zahir al-Riwayah vs. Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah
Describes the first two layers of Hanafi rulings and their sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given Hanafi ruling belongs to the Zahir al-Riwayah or Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah layer and explain its relative authority in the fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
The mufti must weigh rulings: Zahir al-Riwayah is most authoritative; Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah is secondary.

As a mufti, you will encounter Hanafi rulings from various sources. Not all carry the same weight. This lesson introduces the two foundational layers: the strongly transmitted Zahir al-Riwayah from Imam Muhammad's six books, and the less authoritative Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah from other works or weaker chains. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for issuing sound fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first layer: Zahir al-Riwayah
This is the most authoritative layer. It comes from the six core books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir. These are transmitted through well-known, reliable chains.
Sometimes called Masail al-Usul or Riwayat al-Usul.
2
Identify the second layer: Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah
This layer is less authoritative. It includes three subcategories: (1) rulings from Imam Muhammad's other books (e.g., al-Ruqqiyyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, al-Kisaniyyat), (2) rulings from other early Hanafi scholars like Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad, and (3) rulings transmitted through weak or solitary chains (e.g., Nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur).
Also called Riwayat al-Nawadir.
3
Differentiate the chains of transmission
Zahir al-Riwayah is narrated from Imam Muhammad by authoritative students through the six books, ensuring strong thubut (certainty of transmission). Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah comes from lesser-known routes or solitary narrators, making it weaker.
The 'three scholars' (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) are the primary authorities for Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Apply the hierarchy in fatwa practice
When issuing a fatwa, the mufti must first check for a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling. If none exists, he may move to Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah. In case of conflict, the stronger layer prevails.
This hierarchy is a key principle of Rasm al-Mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يم المفتى فى حل من
(۸۳)
شي عقود رسم المفر
ساتواں اصول
مفتی کا مسائل احناف کے طبقات سے واقف ہونا
فقہ حنفی کے بعض مسائل پر ظاہر الروایہ بعض مسائل پر غیر ظاہر الروایہ اور بعض مسائل پر فتاوی کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے اور یہ تینوں مسائل قوت کے اعتبار سے ایک دوسرے سے بڑھے ہوئے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دیتے وقت اس بات کا لحاظ رکھنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ جس قول پر وہ فتوی دے رہا ہے فقہ حنفی میں اس کا مقام و مرتبہ کیا ہے اور طبقات میں اس کی سندی حیثیت کیا ہے۔ مسائل احناف کے تین طبقات
مشہور قول کے مطابق فقہ حنفی کے مسائل کے تین طبقات ہیں جو درج ذیل ہیں:
پہلا طبقہ: ظاہر الروایہ
مسائل کے پہلے طبقہ پر ظاہر الروایہ ، مسائل الاصول اور رولیۃ الاصول کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے اور اس طبقہ میں ان مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جو امام محمد کی چھ کتابوں یعنی مبسوط، جامع صغیر، جامع کبیر، زیادات، سیر صغیر اور سیر کبیر میں اصحاب مذہب سے منقول ہیں، چوں کہ یہ مسائل امام محمد سے مشہور و معروف طریقہ سے منقول ہیں اور ان مسائل کو نقل کرنے والے معتبر اور ثقہ افراد ہیں، اس لئے ان مسائل کو ظاہر الروایہ کہا جاتا ہے اور اسی لئے ان کی استنادی حیثیت دوسرے مسائل کی بہ نسبت زیادہ ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ اصحاب مذہب سے مراد احناف کے علماء ثلاثہ یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد ہیں، بسا اوقات اصحاب مذہب میں ان کے ساتھ امام زفر حسن بن زیاد اور ان کے علاوہ ان فقہاء کو بھی شامل کر لیا جاتا ہے جنھوں نے امام ابوحنیفہ سے علم فقہ حاصل کیا ہے، لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کے سلسلہ میں غالب اور مروج بات یہی ہے کہ وہ یا تو علماء ثلاثہ کا متفق علیہ قول ہوتا ہے یا ان میں سے کسی ایک کا قول ہوتا ہے۔

دوسرا طبقہ: غیر ظاہر الروایہ
مسائل کا دوسرا طبقہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ اور روایۃ النوادر کہلاتا ہے، اس طبقہ میں تین قسم
کے مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جو درج ذیل ہیں:
۱۔ وہ مسائل جو امام محمد کی مذکورہ کتابوں کے علاوہ امام محمد کی دوسری کتابوں یعنی رقیات، جرجانیات، ہارونیات اور کیسانیات وغیرہ میں منقول ہوں۔ فائدہ رقیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے رقہ شہر میں منصب قضاء پر فائز رہنے کے زمانہ میں جمع کیا تھا، ان مسائل کو آپ کے واسطے سے محمد بن سماعہ نے روایت کیا ہے، جرجانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے جُز جان شہر میں جمع کیا تھا، ان مسائل کو آپ کے واسطے سے علی بن صالح جرجانی نے روایت کیا ہے، ہارونیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں جمع کیا تھا، بعض فقہاء کے بقول مسائل کا جو مجموعہ آپ نے ہارون نامی شخص کے لئے جمع کیا تھا ان کو ہارونیات کہا جاتا ہے، کیسانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام ابو عمر وسلیمان بن شعیب بن سلیمان کیسانی (متوفی: ۲۷۸ھ) نے امام محمد کے واسطے سے نقل کیا ہے، یا ایک ضعیف قول کے مطابق مسائل کا وہ مجموعہ جو امام محمد نے شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا تھا اس کو کیسانیات کہا جاتا ہے اور ان دونوں اقوال میں تطبیق بھی دی جاسکتی ہے، بایں طور کہ امام محمد نے اس مجموعہ کو شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا ہو جس کو نقل کرنے والے امام کیسانی ہوں ۔ ( آسان اصول افتاء، دسواں باب)
۲۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم کے دیگر تلامذہ جیسے امام ابویوسف ، امام زفر اور حسن بن زیاد و غیرہ کی کتابوں میں منقول ہوں ۔
۳۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم سے غیر معروف طریقہ سے منقول ہوں یا ان کو نقل کرنے والے تنہا ہوں، جیسے معلی بن منصور، ہشام بن عبید اللہ اور ابن رستم المروزی کی نوادرات۔
Knowledge of the mufti regarding the layers of Hanafi rulings. Some Hanafi rulings are termed Zahir al-Riwayah, some Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, and some Fatawa. These three types differ in strength. Therefore when giving a fatwa, it is necessary to consider the status and authenticity of the ruling within the Hanafi school. According to the well-known view, there are three layers of Hanafi rulings:

First layer: Zahir al-Riwayah. This layer is also called Masail al-Usul and Riwayat al-Usul. It includes rulings transmitted from the founders of the school in the six books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. Because these rulings are transmitted from Imam Muhammad through well-known and authentic channels, they are called Zahir al-Riwayah and have higher evidentiary value. The founders (as-hab al-madhhab) primarily refer to the three scholars: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Sometimes Imam Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and other students of Abu Hanifa are included. However, for Zahir al-Riwayah, the dominant view is that it is either a consensus of the three scholars or the opinion of one of them.

Second layer: Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah or Riwayat al-Nawadir. This includes three types of rulings:
1. Rulings transmitted in Imam Muhammad's other books besides the six, such as al-Ruqqiyyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, and al-Kisaniyyat. Explanation: al-Ruqqiyyat refers to rulings compiled by Imam Muhammad while he was a judge in Raqqa, transmitted by Muhammad ibn Sam'ah. al-Jurjaniyyat refers to rulings compiled in Juzjan, transmitted by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani. al-Haruniyyat refers to rulings compiled during Harun al-Rashid's reign (or for a person named Harun, according to some). al-Kisaniyyat refers to rulings transmitted by Imam Abu Umar Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb al-Kisani (d. 278 AH) from Imam Muhammad, or according to a weak opinion, compiled in the city of Kisan; both views can be reconciled. (Asan Usul al-Ifta, chapter 10)
2. Rulings transmitted in the books of other students of Imam Abu Hanifa, such as Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad.
3. Rulings transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa through less known chains or by solitary narrators, such as the Nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur, Hisham ibn Ubaydullah, and Ibn Rustam al-Marwazi.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a methodology lesson for the mufti on the hierarchical layers of Hanafi rulings. It emphasizes that not all Hanafi rulings carry equal weight; the mufti must distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah (the most authentic layer), Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah (nawadir), and later fatawa. The first layer, Zahir al-Riwayah, derives from the six core works of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. These are the books that form the foundation of the Hanafi madhhab and are transmitted through reliable chains. The second layer, Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, includes rulings from other works of Imam Muhammad or from other early Hanafi authorities, but with less authoritative chains. The passage lists three categories within this second layer: rulings from Imam Muhammad's other compilations (like al-Ruqqiyyat), rulings from other senior students of Abu Hanifa (like Abu Yusuf and Zufar), and rulings transmitted through weak or solitary chains. The author stresses that the mufti must be aware of these layers to properly assign weight to different opinions when issuing fatwas. This classification is essential for understanding the internal hierarchy of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The most authoritative layer of Hanafi rulings, transmitted from Imam Muhammad's six books through well-known and reliable chains.
غیر ظاہر الروایہ (Ghair Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The second layer of Hanafi rulings, less authoritative, including narrations from other books of Imam Muhammad or other early scholars, and weak transmissions.
روایۃ النوادر (Riwāyat al-Nawādir): Synonym for Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, referring to rare transmissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is considered a source of Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) Al-Mabsut
B) Al-Jami' al-Kabir
C) Al-Ruqqiyyat
D) Al-Siyar al-Saghir

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti must distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah (six books of Imam Muhammad) and Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah (other sources) to assign proper weight to rulings.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Third Level of Fatwa: Fatwa, Waqiat, and Takhrijat
Defines the third level of fatwa sources in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third level of fatwa sources in Hanafi iftaa and explain how later mujtahids contribute to the madhhab.

Core Idea
Later mujtahids' ijtihad, when no direct text exists, is valid fatwa within the Hanafi school.

In Hanafi iftaa, rulings are ranked by authority. The highest is Zahir al-Riwayah, then Nawadir, and finally the third level: fatwa, waqiat, and takhrijat of later scholars. This lesson explores who these scholars are and why their opinions matter, even when they differ from the founders.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the hierarchy of fatwa sources
Identify the three levels: Zahir al-Riwayah (core texts), Nawadir (rare transmissions), and the third level (fatwa, waqiat, takhrijat of later mashayikh). Understand that each level has decreasing authority but remains binding in the madhhab.
2
Define the third level components
Distinguish between fatwa (general rulings), waqiat (incident-specific rulings), and takhrijat (derived rulings). All are produced by later mujtahids when direct texts are silent.
Takhrij is a method of extending principles from the madhhab's texts.
3
Identify the scholars of this level
Note the names: direct students of Sahibayn (Isam ibn Yusuf, Ibrahim al-Marwazi, etc.) and their students (Muhammad ibn Salama, Nasir ibn Yahya, etc.). These are the later mujtahids.
Their biographies are found in tabaqat works.
4
Understand intra-madhhab disagreement
These scholars sometimes oppose the founders based on evidence, yet their rulings remain within the Hanafi school. This shows the dynamic nature of the madhhab.
The key rasm rule: later ijtihad is valid and expands the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يم المفتى فى حل من
(۸۵)
شي عقود رسم المف
تیسرا طبقہ: فتاوی اور واقعات
مسائل کے تیسرے طبقہ پر فتاوی، واقعات اور تخریجات مشائخ کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے، اس طبقہ میں ان مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جن کا استنباط مجہتدین متاخرین نے اس وقت کیا جب ان سے ان مسائل کی بابت سوال کیا گیا اور انہوں نے ان مسائل کا جواب اپنے امام کی کتابوں میں نہیں پایا تو بذات خود اجتہاد کر کے ان کا جواب دیا، ان مسائل کو مستنبط کرنے والے صاحبین کے بالواسطہ یا بلا واسطہ شاگرد ہوتے ہیں، ان کی تعداد بہت زیادہ ہے اور ان کے تفصیلی احوال جاننے کے لئے ہمارے اصحاب کی طبقات اور تاریخ کی کتابیں ہیں۔ صاحبین کے شاگردوں میں عصام بن یوسف، ابراہیم بن رستم المروزی، محمد بن سماعه ابوسليمان الجوز جانی اور ابو حفص البخاری کے اسماء قابل ذکر ہیں اور صاحبین کے شاگردوں کے شاگردوں میں محمد بن سلمہ محمد بن مقاتل بنصیر بن یحیی اور ابوالنصر قاسم بن سلام کے اسماء تذکرہ کے قابل ہیں، یہ حضرات بسا اوقات دلائل میں غور و فکر کی بنیاد پر اصحاب مذہب کی مخالفت بھی کرتے ہیں اور ان کے اقوال مذہب سے خارج نہیں کہلاتے ہیں۔
شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٦٧-٧١)
The third level: Fatwa, incidents, and takhrijat of the scholars. The third level of issues includes fatwa, incidents, and takhrijat of the mashayikh. This level includes issues derived by later mujtahids when they were asked about them, and they did not find the answers in their imam's books, so they independently performed ijtihad and answered them. The derivators of these issues are the direct or indirect students of the Sahibayn, and their number is very large. To know their detailed biographies, there are books of tabaqat and history of our companions. Among the students of the Sahibayn, the names of Isam ibn Yusuf, Ibrahim ibn Rustam al-Marwazi, Muhammad ibn Sama'a Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, and Abu Hafs al-Bukhari are noteworthy. And among the students of the students of the Sahibayn, the names of Muhammad ibn Salama, Muhammad ibn Muqatil, Nasir ibn Yahya, and Abu al-Nasr Qasim ibn Salam are worthy of mention. These gentlemen sometimes oppose the founders of the madhhab based on reflection on evidences, and their statements are not considered outside the madhhab. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 67-71)
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage defines the third level of fatwa sources in the Hanafi madhhab. It explains that fatwa, waqiat (incidents), and takhrijat (derived rulings) of later mashayikh belong to this level. These are issues that later mujtahids derived independently when they could not find direct rulings in the books of their imam. The derivators are students or later generations of students of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The passage lists notable scholars from both the immediate students and the next generation. It also notes that these scholars sometimes issue rulings that contradict the founders of the madhhab based on their own examination of evidence, yet their opinions are still considered part of the Hanafi school. This is a key rasm rule: later ijtihad within the madhhab is valid and expands the school's corpus.

Key Terms
طبقہ ثالث (tabaqa thalitha): The third level of fatwa sources, comprising fatwa, waqiat, and takhrijat of later scholars.
تخریجات مشائخ (takhrijat al-mashayikh): Rulings derived by later scholars through extension or deduction from existing texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the third level of fatwa in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah
B) Fatwa based on Nawadir
C) Fatwa based on fatwa, waqiat, and takhrijat of later scholars
D) Fatwa based on the consensus of the Sahibayn

Key Takeaway
The third level of fatwa—fatwa, waqiat, and takhrijat—is a valid and essential part of the Hanafi madhhab, allowing it to address new issues through the ijtihad of later scholars.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
