The Authority of Early Jurists' Tarjih
Rasm al-Mufti rule on following early tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a mufti must follow the tarjih of the mutqaddimin even if they were muqallid, and explain the rationale based on the sources.

Core Idea
The tarjih of early Hanafi jurists is binding, even if they were not independent mujtahids.

When there is no explicit statement from the early giants of the madhhab, later muftis must defer to their preferences — not because those scholars were infallible, but because their choices were grounded in deep knowledge of the sources. This principle preserves the integrity of the madhhab across generations. In this lesson, you will trace the reasoning behind this authoritative rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject
Who does this rule address? Find the party obligated to follow the tarjih.
It applies to muftis (later scholars issuing fatwas).
2
Identify the Scope
Under what conditions must this tarjih be followed? The passage specifies 'issues for which there is no explicit statement from the mutqaddimin.'
It does not apply when the early jurists have already given an explicit text (nass).
3
Identify the Ruling
What exactly is required? Following their tarjih (preference) is necessary (lazim).
Even if the early jurists were muqallids (not independent mujtahids).
4
Extract the Rationale (Talil)
Why is this rule imposed? The passage gives two reasons: (1) their tarjih was not based on conjecture but on knowledge of sources, (2) their writings testify to this.
The authority comes from their method, not their personal ijtihad status.
5
Assess the Authority Level
Where does this rule sit in the Hanafi hierarchy? It is from later fatawa (sharh of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti), but it reflects a principle implicit in the classical works.
Considered mufta bihi (operative) for modern fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسائل جن کے بارے میں متقدمین سے کوئی صراحت نہیں ہے اور ان کی ترجیحات میں بھی ان کی پیروی کرنا لازم ہے، اگر چہ یہ فقہاء کسی غیر مجتہد کے قول کو ہی راجح قرار دیں، جیسا کہ ہم نے اس بات کو اس بحث کے آغاز میں بیان کر دیا ہے، اس لئے کہ ان لوگوں نے جس قول کو راج قرار دیا ہے محض اٹکل سے اس کو راج نہیں قرار دیا ہے، بلکہ ان کے مآخذ سے واقف ہونے کے بعد ہی اسے ترجیح دی ہے، جیسا کہ ان کی تصنیفات اس بات پر شاہد ہیں۔
Regarding issues for which there is no explicit statement from the early jurists (mutqaddimin), it is necessary to follow their preferences (tarjih), even if these jurists declared a saying of a non-mujtahid as preponderant. As we have explained at the beginning of this discussion, because these people did not declare a saying as preponderant merely by conjecture, but rather they gave preference after being acquainted with its sources, as their writings testify to this.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti principle from the sharh of Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. It establishes that a mufti must adhere to the tarjih (preference) made by the early Hanafi jurists (mutqaddimin) even if those jurists themselves were not independent mujtahids (i.e., they were muqallids within the madhhab). The reasoning is that their tarjih was not arbitrary; it was based on deep knowledge of the sources (makhadh) of the madhhab. Therefore, later muftis, even if more knowledgeable in other respects, cannot override these established preferences. This principle ensures consistency and authority within the madhhab.

Key Terms
متقدمین (mutqaddimin): The early jurists of the Hanafi madhhab, from the time of the founding imams up to the period of the later scholars (mutakhkhirin).
ترجیح (tarjih): The act of preferring one legal opinion over another based on evidences or principles.
راجح (rajih): Preponderant or preferred opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why must a mufti follow the tarjih of the mutqaddimin even if they were muqallid?
A) Because they were independent mujtahids.
B) Because their preferences were based on sound knowledge of sources.
C) Because later scholars cannot override them.
D) Because of ijma'.

Key Takeaway
The tarjih of early Hanafi jurists is binding on later muftis because it is grounded in deep source knowledge, not personal opinion.

The Eleventh Principle: Answering Non-Textual Cases
Procedure for mufti when no explicit ruling exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of steps a mufti must follow when no explicit ruling exists (ghayr mansus) and apply it to a hypothetical scenario.

Core Idea
A mufti must not rely on personal opinion when texts are silent; follow hierarchy: principles, consensus, ijtihad, or most learned.

This lesson introduces the eleventh principle of mufti methodology: how to handle cases not explicitly found in the transmitted corpus of the madhhab. The passage synthesizes guidance from Allamah Shami and Fatawa Qadi Khan to provide a clear hierarchy that safeguards the fatwa process from conjecture. Understanding this principle is essential for anyone involved in issuing fatwas within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize when a case has no explicit ruling from the imams or later scholars (ghayr mansus).
2
Check ghayr zahir al-riwaya
If the issue is from ghayr zahir al-riwaya (transmitted outside the six core books), check if it conforms to the principles of the imams; if so, act on it.
This step takes priority over later consensus.
3
Check consensus of later scholars
If no narration from imams exists, see if later scholars (mutakhkhirin) have a consensus; follow that.
Their agreement is binding.
4
Handle disagreement among later scholars
If later scholars disagree, a mujtahid mufti may perform ijtihad and give the ruling he deems correct.
Only a mujtahid can do this.
5
If mufti is a muqallid
If the mufti is not a mujtahid, he must follow the most learned scholar (afqah) available, even contacting by letter if necessary.
He attributes the fatwa to that scholar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مفتی کے سامنے کبھی کبھی ایسا واقعہ بھی پیش آتا ہے جس میں امام اعظم، صاحبین، مشائخ مذہب اور دیگر متقدمین و متاخرین فقہاء سے کوئی صریح قول منقول نہیں ہوتا ہے، تو اس واقعہ کی بابت مفتی کے لئے اپنی رائے پر فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا یا نہیں؟ علامہ شامی اس سوال کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں: اور اگر بعد کے مشائخ سے بھی قطعاً کوئی صریح حکم مروی نہ ہو، تو مفتی اس واقعہ میں خوب غور و فکر اور کوشش کرے، تا کہ وہ اس مسئلہ کا کوئی ایسا حکم دریافت کر سکے جس کے ذریعہ وہ اپنی ذمہ داری سے عہدہ برآ ہو سکے، اور اپنے منصب اور اس کی حرمت کے پیش نظر اس مسئلہ میں اٹکل سے گفتگو نہ کرے، اور اللہ تعالی سے ڈرے اور اس کا خوف رکھے، کیوں کہ فتوی دینا نہایت اہم معاملہ ہے، اس کی جسارت وہی کرتا ہے جو جاہل اور بد بخت ہوتا ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۲۱) فتاوی قاضی خان میں ہے: اگر کوئی مسئلہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو تو اگر وہ مسئلہ ہمارے ائمہ کے اصول وضوابط کے موافق ہو تو مفتی اس پر عمل کرے، اور اگر کوئی مفتی کسی مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ سے کوئی روایت نہ پائے اور اس مسئلہ میں متاخرین کسی بات پر متفق ہوں تو مفتی اسی پر عمل کرے، اور اگر ان کا اختلاف ہو تو مفتی اجتہاد کرے، اور اس کے نزدیک جو بات درست ہو اسی پر فتوی دے، اور اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہو تو اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہو اس کے قول کو اختیار کرے اور جواب کو اسی کی طرف منسوب کرے، پس اگر اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہے وہ دوسرے شہر میں رہتا ہو تو اس سے خط کے ذریعہ رابطہ کرے، اور اس کے
Sometimes a situation occurs before the mufti for which no explicit statement is transmitted from Imam A'zam, the Sahibayn, the mashayikh of the madhhab, and other early and later jurists. So regarding that situation, is it permissible for the mufti to give a fatwa based on his own opinion? Allamah Shami answers this question, saying: 'And if no explicit ruling is transmitted at all even from later mashayikh, then the mufti should deeply ponder and strive in that situation, so that he may discover some ruling for that issue by which he can fulfill his responsibility. And, considering his position and its sanctity, he should not speak about this issue based on conjecture. He should fear Allah and hold awe of Him, because giving fatwa is a very serious matter; only the ignorant and ill-fated dare to do it.' (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, 121) In Fatawa Qadikhan: 'If an issue is from ghayr zahir al-riwaya, then if that issue is in accordance with the principles and regulations of our imams, the mufti should act upon it. And if a mufti finds no narration from our imams in an issue, and in that issue the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) are agreed upon something, then the mufti should act upon that. If they disagree, then the mufti should exercise ijtihad, and give fatwa on whatever he finds correct. If the mufti is a muqallid and not a mujtahid, then he should adopt the saying of the person who is more learned (afqah) in his view, and attribute the answer to him. Then if that person who is more learned in his view lives in another city, he should contact him by letter.' [and he]
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage introduces the eleventh principle of mufti methodology: how to handle cases that are not explicitly found in the transmitted texts of the madhhab (ghayr mansus). The text presents two authoritative sources. First, Allamah Shami's guidance: if no explicit ruling exists from any scholar of the madhhab, the mufti must exert maximum effort (ijtihad) to derive a ruling, always fearing Allah and avoiding conjecture. Second, Fatawa Qadi Khan provides a detailed hierarchy: 1. For issues from ghayr zahir al-riwaya (i.e., transmitted but not in the six core books), if the issue conforms to the principles of the imams, act accordingly. 2. If no narration from the imams exists, follow the consensus of the later scholars (mutakhkhirin). 3. If later scholars disagree, the mufti must make ijtihad and give the ruling he deems correct. 4. If the mufti is a muqallid (not a mujtahid), he must follow the opinion of the most learned scholar available, even if that scholar is in another city, contacting him by letter. This principle ensures that fatwas are grounded in the madhhab's methodology even when direct texts are absent.

Key Terms
غیر منصوص (ghayr mansus): A legal case for which no explicit textual ruling is found in the transmitted corpus of the madhhab.
اجتہاد (ijtihad): Independent reasoning by a qualified person to derive a ruling from the sources or principles of the madhhab.
مفتی مقلد (mufti muqallid): A mufti who does not have the ability to perform ijtihad and must adhere to the rulings of the madhhab's scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mufti finds no explicit ruling from the imams and later scholars disagree on an issue, what should a mufti who is a mujtahid do?
A) Pick the opinion of the oldest scholar.
B) Make ijtihad and give the ruling he deems correct.
C) Refrain from giving a fatwa.
D) Refer the matter to the founding imams' qiyas.

Key Takeaway
When no explicit ruling exists, the mufti must follow a hierarchy: check transmitted texts, then consensus of later scholars, then ijtihad (if mujtahid) or follow the most learned scholar (if muqallid).

8 min
The Rarity of Missing a Ruling in Hanafi Works
Quoting Allama Shami's reassurance to muftis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that no incident is missing from the Hanafi school to guide a mufti's research and avoid premature claims of unprecedented cases.

Core Idea
No incident is truly missing from the Hanafi books — either the exact ruling or a general maxim applies.

Allama Shami provides a crucial reassurance for muftis who struggle to find a direct ruling. This principle builds confidence in the comprehensiveness of the Hanafi school. In this lesson, you will understand why a mufti's failure to find a ruling is usually due to insufficient research, not a gap in the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the mufti's anxiety
Recognize that a mufti may worry when a direct ruling is not immediately found, fearing the case is unprecedented.
This principle addresses that fear.
2
Identify the two reasons for missing a ruling
Shami states the dominant assumption: lack of research or ignorance of where the ruling is recorded.
Never assume the school is incomplete.
3
Recognize the underlying assumption
The Hanafi school is comprehensive; it is extremely rare for a case to have no mention.
This is a foundational premise for fatwa methodology.
4
Distinguish the two forms of coverage
Either the exact case is recorded, or a general legal maxim (qāʿida kulliyya) applies.
General maxims expand the school's reach.
5
Apply the principle to research practice
When a ruling is not found, the mufti should intensify search, check indexes, and consult general maxims before concluding it's missing.
This principle encourages thoroughness and reliance on the school's riches.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامہ شامی مزید فرماتے ہیں: (شرح عقود رسم المفتی : ۱۲۲) اور غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ مفتی کا کسی مسئلہ میں عبارت (یعنی فقہاء کے اقوال ) کا نہ پانا اس کی جستجو کی کمی کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے یا اس وجہ سے ہوتا ہے کہ اسے اس مقام کا پتہ ہی نہیں ہوتا جہاں وہ مسئلہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے، کیوں کہ یہ امر بہت نادر اور شاذ ہے کہ کوئی واقعہ پیش آئے اور کتب مذہب میں اس کا ذکر نہ ہو، یا تو بعینہ وہی مسئلہ مذکور ہوتا ہے، یا کوئی ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ مذکور ہوتا ہے جو اس واقعہ کو بھی شامل ہوتا ہے۔(شرح عقود رسم المفتی:۱۲۳)
Allama Shami further says: (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 122) And the dominant assumption is that a mufti's not finding an expression (i.e., the statements of jurists) on a certain issue is due to his lack of research or due to not knowing the place where that issue is mentioned, because it is very rare and unusual that an incident occurs and there is no mention of it in the books of the school. Either that very issue is mentioned, or some general maxim is mentioned that includes that incident. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 123)
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule (methodological principle) for muftis, quoted from Allama Shami's commentary on Rasm al-Mufti. It addresses the anxiety of a mufti who cannot find a direct ruling. Shami reassures that the Hanafi school is comprehensive. If a mufti fails to find an explicit ruling, it is either because he did not search thoroughly or because he does not know where to look. The underlying assumption is that no novel case is truly unprecedented; either the exact case is recorded, or a general legal maxim (qāʿida kulliyya) applies. This principle encourages scholarly diligence and trust in the school's literature.

Key Terms
عبارت (ibārat): In this context, the actual wording/saying of the jurists (fuqahā) regarding a specific issue.
قاعده کلیه (qāʿida kulliyya): A general legal maxim that can govern multiple specific cases.
نادر و شاذ (nādir wa shādh): Extremely rare and unusual; describing the likelihood of a case missing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allama Shami, if a mufti cannot find a ruling in the books of the Hanafi school, what is the most likely reason?
A) The case is truly unprecedented and requires independent ijtihad
B) The mufti lacks proper research skills or does not know the source
C) The Hanafi school is incomplete
D) The mufti should refer to another school

Key Takeaway
A mufti must assume that any case is covered in the school's literature, either explicitly or through a general maxim, and therefore should search thoroughly before concluding otherwise.

The Principle of Mafhum Mukhalif: Interpreting Qualified Fiqh Statements
Explanation of the principle of opposite meaning with a talaq example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of mafhum mukhalif to derive the opposite ruling when a fiqh text qualifies a ruling with a condition or attribute.

Core Idea
When a ruling is tied to a condition, the absence of that condition yields the opposite ruling.

This lesson introduces a fundamental tool for muftis: the principle of mafhum mukhalif (opposite meaning). Fiqh books often attach conditions or descriptions to rulings. The mufti must understand that these qualifications are not accidental; they intentionally signal that the ruling changes when the qualification is absent. We will see this through a classic example from the chapter of divorce and then articulate the principle clearly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qualification
Look at the fiqh text and identify any condition, attribute, or description attached to the ruling. In the example, the wife is described as 'madkhul biha' (consummated).
2
State the ruling for the qualified case
Note the ruling given when the qualification is present. In the example: three divorces occur when saying 'anti taliq' three times to a consummated wife without emphasis.
3
Apply mafhum mukhalif
The principle dictates that when the qualification is absent, the opposite ruling applies. Here, for a non-consummated wife, the ruling is the opposite: only one divorce occurs, and it is bain.
This principle is not automatic for every description; it must be intended as a condition (shart).
4
Derive the complete ruling
Combine both rulings to form a complete picture. The mufti must know both cases to issue correct fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بارہواں اصول
مفتی کا مفہوم مخالف کا اعتبار کرنا

فقہی کتابوں کا ایک خاص اسلوب ہوتا ہے جس کے تحت شرعی مسائل کو نقل کیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ عبارت میں کسی مسئلہ کو کسی شرط یا صفت وغیرہ کی قید سے مقید کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس صفت اور شرط کے نہ پائے جانے کی صورت میں دونوں کا حکم الگ الگ ہوگا۔ مثلا فقہی کتابوں میں ایک مسئلہ لکھا ہوا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص اپنی مدخولہ بیوی سے انت طالق انت طالق انت طالق کہے اور تاکید کی نیت نہ ہو تو اس کی بیوی پر تین طلاق واقع ہوگی تو اس عبارت میں مدخولہ کی قید سے اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ بیوی اگر غیر مدخول بہا ہو تو تین طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی بلکہ ایک ہی طلاق سے وہ بائنہ ہو جائے گی۔
لہذا ایک مفتی کے لئے نصوص اور فقہی عبارات کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے طریقہ کار کو سمجھنا انتہائی ضروری امر ہے ، ذیل میں اس ضابطہ کی مزید تشریح کی جاتی ہے: معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے نصوص کے اقسام
فقہاء احناف کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے ۴ قسمیں ہیں جو درج ذیل ہیں : عبارة النص ، اشارۃ النص، دلالۃ النص اور اقتضاء النص ، جب کہ شوافع اور دیگر اصولیین کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے صرف ۲ قسمیں ہیں: منطوق اور مفہوم ۔
ذیل میں ان میں سے ہر ایک قسم کا مختصر تعارف مع مثال کے تحریر کیا جارہا ہے۔
Twelfth Principle: The Mufti's Consideration of the Opposite Meaning

Fiqh books have a special style by which legal issues are transmitted. Accordingly, qualifying an issue in the text with a condition or attribute etc. means that in the absence of that attribute and condition, the ruling for both is different. For example, in fiqh books, an issue is written: if a person says to his wife who is madkhul biha (consummated) 'anti taliq, anti taliq, anti taliq' and did not intend emphasis, three divorces occur. In this text, the qualification of 'madkhul biha' indicates that if the wife is not madkhul biha, three divorces will not occur; rather, one divorce will occur and she will become bain (irrevocably separated).
Therefore, for a mufti, understanding the method of textual indication of nusus (texts) and fiqh expressions upon their meanings is extremely necessary. Below, further explanation of this principle is given: Types of Texts with regard to indication of meaning.
According to Hanafi jurists, texts are of four types with regard to indication of meaning: 'ibarah al-nass (explicit meaning), isharah al-nass (alluded meaning), dalalah al-nass (inferred meaning), and iqtida' al-nass (implied meaning). Whereas according to the Shafi'is and other usuliyyun, texts are of only two types with regard to indication of meaning: mantiq (explicit statement) and mafhum (implicit understanding).
Below, a brief introduction with examples of each type is being written.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage introduces a critical rule for muftis: when a fiqh text attaches a condition or description to a ruling, the mufti must understand that the opposite ruling applies when that condition is absent. This is the concept of 'mafhum al-mukhalafah' (the opposite meaning). The example given is from the chapter of talaq: if a man utters three divorces to his wife without intending emphasis, the rule differs based on whether the wife is madkhul biha (consummated) or not. If she is madkhul biha, three divorces occur; if not, only one divorce occurs and it is bain. This illustrates how a simple qualification changes the ruling entirely. The author then emphasizes that a mufti must understand the method of textual indication, and he lists the four types recognized by the Hanafis: 'ibarah (explicit), isharah (alluded), dalalah (inferred), and iqtida' (implied). He contrasts this with the Shafi'i school, which only recognizes two: mantiq (explicit) and mafhum (implicit). This sets the stage for a detailed study of each type.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum mukhalif): The opposite meaning deduced from a conditional or qualified statement; i.e., when a ruling is tied to a condition, the absence of that condition yields the opposite ruling.
مدخولہ (madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has had sexual intercourse (consummated marriage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a man says 'anti taliq anti taliq anti taliq' to his non-consummated wife without intending emphasis?
A) Three divorces occur.
B) One divorce occurs and she becomes bain.
C) No divorce occurs.
D) Two divorces occur.

Key Takeaway
The principle of mafhum mukhalif is essential for interpreting qualified fiqh texts: the absence of a condition flips the ruling.

Hanafi Classification of Textual Indications: 'Ibarah, Isharah, Dalalah, Iqtida'
Introduction to types of textual indication and the Hanafi-Shafi'i difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four Hanafi types of textual indication and explain why Hanafis distinguish them from the Shafi'i two-type system.

Core Idea
Hanafi usul identifies four types of textual indication for precise fatwa derivation.

This lesson explores the Hanafi classification of how texts indicate their meanings. The passage introduces four categories: 'ibarah (explicit), isharah (alluded), dalalah (inferred), and iqtida' (implied). This is contrasted with the Shafi'i approach, which uses only two categories: mantiq (explicit) and mafhum (implicit). Understanding this classification helps a mufti recognize the depth of textual implications and avoid oversimplification.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the four Hanafi categories
The four types are: 'ibarah al-nass (explicit meaning), isharah al-nass (alluded meaning), dalalah al-nass (inferred meaning), iqtida' al-nass (implied meaning). Each provides a different level of legal evidence.
These categories are hierarchical in strength.
2
Understand the Shafi'i alternative
Shafi'is and other usuliyyun only use two categories: mantiq (explicit statement) and mafhum (implicit understanding). They subsume the Hanafi four under these two.
3
Identify the practical difference
The Hanafi four allow for more nuanced derivation of rulings from texts, as each category has distinct rules. The Shafi'i two are broader.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) may appear in complex istinbat scenarios.
4
Apply the categories to a text
Take a Quranic verse or hadith and determine which of the four categories applies. This requires practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بارہواں اصول
مفتی کا مفہوم مخالف کا اعتبار کرنا

فقہی کتابوں کا ایک خاص اسلوب ہوتا ہے جس کے تحت شرعی مسائل کو نقل کیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ عبارت میں کسی مسئلہ کو کسی شرط یا صفت وغیرہ کی قید سے مقید کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس صفت اور شرط کے نہ پائے جانے کی صورت میں دونوں کا حکم الگ الگ ہوگا۔ مثلا فقہی کتابوں میں ایک مسئلہ لکھا ہوا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص اپنی مدخولہ بیوی سے انت طالق انت طالق انت طالق کہے اور تاکید کی نیت نہ ہو تو اس کی بیوی پر تین طلاق واقع ہوگی تو اس عبارت میں مدخولہ کی قید سے اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ بیوی اگر غیر مدخول بہا ہو تو تین طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی بلکہ ایک ہی طلاق سے وہ بائنہ ہو جائے گی۔
لہذا ایک مفتی کے لئے نصوص اور فقہی عبارات کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے طریقہ کار کو سمجھنا انتہائی ضروری امر ہے ، ذیل میں اس ضابطہ کی مزید تشریح کی جاتی ہے: معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے نصوص کے اقسام
فقہاء احناف کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے ۴ قسمیں ہیں جو درج ذیل ہیں : عبارة النص ، اشارۃ النص، دلالۃ النص اور اقتضاء النص ، جب کہ شوافع اور دیگر اصولیین کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے صرف ۲ قسمیں ہیں: منطوق اور مفہوم ۔
ذیل میں ان میں سے ہر ایک قسم کا مختصر تعارف مع مثال کے تحریر کیا جارہا ہے۔
Twelfth Principle: The Mufti's Consideration of the Opposite Meaning

Fiqh books have a special style by which legal issues are transmitted. Accordingly, qualifying an issue in the text with a condition or attribute etc. means that in the absence of that attribute and condition, the ruling for both is different. For example, in fiqh books, an issue is written: if a person says to his wife who is madkhul biha (consummated) 'anti taliq, anti taliq, anti taliq' and did not intend emphasis, three divorces occur. In this text, the qualification of 'madkhul biha' indicates that if the wife is not madkhul biha, three divorces will not occur; rather, one divorce will occur and she will become bain (irrevocably separated).
Therefore, for a mufti, understanding the method of textual indication of nusus (texts) and fiqh expressions upon their meanings is extremely necessary. Below, further explanation of this principle is given: Types of Texts with regard to indication of meaning.
According to Hanafi jurists, texts are of four types with regard to indication of meaning: 'ibarah al-nass (explicit meaning), isharah al-nass (alluded meaning), dalalah al-nass (inferred meaning), and iqtida' al-nass (implied meaning). Whereas according to the Shafi'is and other usuliyyun, texts are of only two types with regard to indication of meaning: mantiq (explicit statement) and mafhum (implicit understanding).
Below, a brief introduction with examples of each type is being written.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage introduces a critical rule for muftis: when a fiqh text attaches a condition or description to a ruling, the mufti must understand that the opposite ruling applies when that condition is absent. This is the concept of 'mafhum al-mukhalafah' (the opposite meaning). The example given is from the chapter of talaq: if a man utters three divorces to his wife without intending emphasis, the rule differs based on whether the wife is madkhul biha (consummated) or not. If she is madkhul biha, three divorces occur; if not, only one divorce occurs and it is bain. This illustrates how a simple qualification changes the ruling entirely. The author then emphasizes that a mufti must understand the method of textual indication, and he lists the four types recognized by the Hanafis: 'ibarah (explicit), isharah (alluded), dalalah (inferred), and iqtida' (implied). He contrasts this with the Shafi'i school, which only recognizes two: mantiq (explicit) and mafhum (implicit). This sets the stage for a detailed study of each type.

Key Terms
عبارۃ النص ('ibarah al-nass): The explicit meaning derived directly from the wording of the text.
اشارۃ النص (isharah al-nass): The alluded meaning: a meaning not explicitly stated but clearly implied by the text's structure or context.
دلالۃ النص (dalalah al-nass): The inferred meaning: a ruling derived through logical reasoning from the text, often by identifying an underlying cause (illah).
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' al-nass): The implied meaning: an unstated element that is necessary for the text to be coherent or consistent with other principles.
منطوق (mantiq): The explicit statement: the direct meaning of the words themselves.
مفہوم (mafhum): The implicit understanding: any meaning derived beyond the literal words, including mafhum al-muwafaqah (coextensive) and mafhum al-mukhalafah (opposite).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 2
B) 4
C) 3
D) 5

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul classifies textual indication into four types to enable precise derivation of rulings, contrasting with the simpler Shafi'i two-type system.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Mafhum Muwafiq (Fahwa al-Khitab): Deriving Stronger or Equal Rulings
Defines Mafhum Muwafiq with two Quranic examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a case of Mafhum Muwafiq in a Quranic verse or hadith, distinguish it from Mafhum Mukhalif, and apply the principle to derive the ruling for an unstated case.

Core Idea
When text prohibits a lesser act, it prohibits a greater act with stronger priority.

This lesson introduces Mafhum Muwafiq (Fahwa al-Khitab), a key principle of textual interpretation in Hanafi usul. You will learn how the implied tone of the text extends a ruling to unstated cases with equal or greater force. Two classic Quranic examples will be analyzed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its synonyms
Note that Mafhum Muwafiq is also called Fahwa al-Khitab (tone of address). Understand that it applies when the unstated case carries a ruling that is either stronger (awla) or equal (musawi) to the stated case.
Do not confuse with Mafhum Mukhalif, which gives the opposite ruling.
2
Analyze the first example: parental respect
From Allah's command 'Do not say to them 'uff'' (Quran 17:23), the prohibition of striking parents is derived with greater emphasis. This is a fortiori (awla) Mafhum Muwafiq because if saying 'uff' is prohibited, then striking is even more prohibited.
The logical reasoning: the prohibition of a lesser act implies prohibition of a greater act.
3
Analyze the second example: orphan's wealth
From the verse 'Indeed, those who consume the wealth of orphans unjustly...' (Quran 4:10), the prohibition of burning the orphan's wealth is derived. Here, the ruling is of the same level (musawi) because both consumption and burning are forms of destruction (itlaf).
The essential purpose (maqsad) is to protect orphan's wealth from any harm.
4
Distinguish the two subtypes
The first example is 'awla' (stronger priority), the second is 'musawi' (equal priority). Both fall under Mafhum Muwafiq. Understand that in awla, the unstated case is more deserving of the ruling; in musawi, the ruling applies equally.
Hanafis accept both as valid forms of istinbat.
5
Apply the principle to a new case
Consider the hadith: 'When a dog licks a vessel, wash it seven times, one of them with soil.' Using Mafhum Muwafiq, what ruling can be derived for a pig licking? The greater impurity implies a stronger requirement, so similar or stricter purification would be needed.
This is a common exercise in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کے ارشاد فَلا تَقُلْ لَّهُمَا اُفْ سے مسکوت عنہ یعنی والدین پر دست درازی کی حرمت کا حکم بدرجہ اولی سمجھ میں آتا ہے اور لحن الخطاب یہ ہے کہ نص میں جس صورت کا حکم بیان نہیں کیا گیا ہے اس مسکوت کے لئے منطوق کا حکم برابر درجہ میں ثابت ہوتا ہو، جیسے اللہ تعالی کا ارشاد ہے ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِيْنَ يَأْكُلُونَ أَمْوالَ الْيَتَامَى ظُلْماً (النساء: ۱۰) اس آیت میں ظلماً یتیموں کا مال کھانے پر وعید بیان کی گئی ہے لیکن اس آیت سے یتیموں کا مال جلانے کی وعید بھی سمجھ میں آتی ہے، اس لیے کہ آیت کا اصل مقصد یتیم کے مال کو تلف کرنے سے منع کرنا ہے اور اتلاف دونوں صورتوں میں برابر درجہ کی ہے، پس دونوں حکموں کا ثبوت برابر درجہ میں ہوا۔
From the saying 'Do not say to them 'uff'' (Quran 17:23), the unstated case—i.e., the prohibition of striking parents—is understood with greater priority. And Fahwa al-Khitab (tone of address) is that a ruling for a case not mentioned in the text is established at the same level as the mentioned ruling for the unstated case. For example, Allah's saying: 'Indeed, those who consume the wealth of orphans unjustly...' (Quran 4:10). In this verse, a warning is given for consuming orphans' wealth unjustly, but from this verse the warning for burning orphans' wealth is also understood, because the essential purpose of the verse is to prohibit destroying the orphan's wealth, and destruction is of the same level in both forms. Thus, the proof of both rulings is at the same level.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage defines Mafhum Muwafiq (also called Fahwa al-Khitab), a principle of textual interpretation. According to Hanafi usul, when the text mentions a ruling for a particular case, that ruling applies with even greater force to a more obvious unstated case. The author provides two examples: First, from 'Do not say 'uff'' to parents, the prohibition of striking them is understood a fortiori. Second, from the verse about consuming orphans' wealth, the prohibition of burning it is understood because both are forms of destruction, and the ruling is of the same level. This is a key tool in istinbat (derivation of rulings).

Key Terms
مفہوم موافق (mafhum muwafiq): A ruling for an unstated case that is either stronger or equal to the stated case, derived from the tone or purpose of the text.
فحوی الخطاب (fahwa al-khitab): The implied meaning of the address; another term for Mafhum Muwafiq.
مسکوت عنہ (maskut 'anhu): The unstated case about which the text is silent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the verse 'Do not say to them 'uff'' (Quran 17:23), the prohibition of striking parents is derived through which type of inference?
A) Mafhum Mukhalif
B) Mafhum Muwafiq (Fahwa al-Khitab)
C) Qiyas Khafi
D) Istihsan

Key Takeaway
Mafhum Muwafiq allows a mufti to extend a ruling from a stated case to an unstated case when the unstated case shares or exceeds the underlying purpose of the text.

Validity of Mafhum Mukhalif in Fiqh Narrations
Establishing validity of mafhum mukhalif in fiqh narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when mafhum mukhalif is valid in Hanafi fatwa and apply the distinction between riwayat fiqhiyyah and nusus.

Core Idea
Mafhum mukhalif is a valid proof in fiqh narrations but not in primary texts (nusus).

This lesson establishes a crucial principle for the mufti: the validity of mafhum mukhalif depends on the source type. The Hanafi school draws a sharp line between narrations in fiqh books—where mafhum mukhalif is accepted by consensus—and the Quran and Hadith, where it is not. This distinction shapes how a mufti derives rulings from the transmitted heritage.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the rule
Learn the fundamental rule: mafhum mukhalif is valid in riwayat fiqhiyyah (narrations in fiqh books) by consensus among Hanafis.
2
Identify the exception
Understand that mafhum mukhalif is not valid in nusus (Quran and Hadith). This exception is critical for correct fatwa derivation.
3
Classify Sahaba statements
Separate Companions' statements based on ijtihad and ra'y (treat as fiqh narrations) from those not based on ra'y (treat as marfu' hadith, thus nusus).
If a Companion's statement cannot be known through opinion/ijtihad, it is at the level of a marfu' hadith.
4
Apply the principle
When encountering a conditional or qualified statement in a fiqh narration, derive the opposite ruling. But do not apply this to a hadith or direct Quranic text.
Example: 'Zakat is obligatory on free Muslims who own nisab.' → Mafhum mukhalif: not obligatory on slaves or those who do not own nisab.
5
Note the consensus
The Hanafi school is unanimous on this rule for riwayat fiqhiyyah, as cited from al-Nahr al-Fa'iq and Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
There is no khilaf among Hanafis on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النهر الفائق شرح کنز الدقائق کی کتاب الحج میں ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف روایات میں بالاتفاق معتبر ہے اور صحابہ کے ارشادات بھی اسی ذیل میں آتے ہیں، صاحب نہر نے فرمایا کہ اقوال صحابہ میں یہ قید بڑھانی مناسب ہے کہ وہ اقوال رائے واجتہاد سے جانے جاسکتے ہوں، وہ اقوال مراد نہیں ہیں جو رائے واجتہاد سے نہیں جانے جاسکتے ہوں (کیوں کہ صحابہ کے ایسے اقوال نصوص شرعیہ کے درجہ میں ہیں)۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٥١) علامہ ابن عابدین شامی اس کی مزید وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ صحابہ کے ایسے ارشادات جو رائے و اجتہاد سے نہ جانے جاسکتے ہوں وہ حدیث مرفوع کے حکم میں ہیں اور احادیث میں مفہوم مخالف معتبر نہیں ، پس صاحب نہر کی روایات سے مراد وہ باتیں ہیں جو کتب فقہیہ میں مجتہدین سے مروی ہیں، خواہ وہ مجتہدین صحابہ کرام سے مروی ہوں یا ان کے بعد کے حضرات سے، اور النہر الفائق ہی میں وضو کی سنتوں کے بیان میں ہے کہ کتب فقہیہ میں مفہوم مخالف حجت ہے اور نصوص کے بیشتر مفہومات کا معاملہ اس سے مختلف ہے۔
In the book al-Nahr al-Fa'iq commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, in the book of Hajj, it is stated that mafhum mukhalif (opposite meaning) is accepted in narrations by consensus, and the statements of the Companions also fall under this category. The author of al-Nahr said: In the statements of the Companions, it is appropriate to add this condition: those statements that can be known through opinion and ijtihad (are included); those statements that cannot be known through opinion and ijtihad are not intended (because such statements of the Companions are at the level of legal texts). (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 151) Allama Ibn Abidin al-Shami, further clarifying, says: The statements of the Companions that cannot be known through opinion and ijtihad are in the ruling of marfu' hadith, and mafhum mukhalif is not considered valid in hadiths. Therefore, by 'narrations' (riwayat) in al-Nahr, what is meant are those matters narrated from mujtahids in the fiqh books, whether those mujtahids are from the noble Companions or from later scholars. And in al-Nahr al-Fa'iq itself, in the discussion of the Sunnahs of ablution, it is stated that in fiqh books, mafhum mukhalif is a proof (hujja), while the majority of the concepts from texts (nusus) are different from this.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage establishes a key methodological rule for Hanafi fatwa. The text distinguishes between two types of sources: riwayat fiqhiyyah (narrations in fiqh books, which include statements of mujtahids) and nusus (Quran and Hadith). In the former, mafhum mukhalif (the opposite implication) is valid and can be used as evidence by consensus. In the latter, it is not valid according to the Hanafi school. The passage then addresses the special category of Companion statements. If a Companion's statement is based on ra'y (opinion) and ijtihad, it is treated as a fiqh narration, and mafhum mukhalif applies. If it is not based on ra'y (i.e., it directly conveys something heard from the Prophet), it is treated as a marfu' hadith, in which mafhum mukhalif is not valid. Ibn Abidin clarifies that the 'riwayat' in the Nahr refer to statements of mujtahids recorded in fiqh books, which include the Companions' ijtihad-based statements and those of later scholars.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum mukhalif): The opposite implication derived from a statement; e.g., if a ruling is specified for a particular case, it implies the ruling is different for other cases.
روایات فقہیہ (riwayat fiqhiyyah): Narrations in fiqh books from mujtahids, including Companions' ijtihad-based statements.
نصوص (nusus): Primary texts of Quran and mutawatir/ahad hadith that are not open to ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which type of source is mafhum mukhalif considered valid?
A) Quran and Sunnah (nusus)
B) Fiqh narrations (riwayat fiqhiyyah)
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Mafhum mukhalif is a valid proof in fiqh narrations (including Companions' ijtihad-based statements) but not in primary texts (Quran and Hadith).

The Validity of Mafhum Mukhalif in Hanafi Fatwa Practice
Ruling and debate on mafhum mukhalif inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions within the Hanafi school on mafhum mukhalif and apply the mufta bihi position in fatwa reasoning.

Core Idea
Mafhum mukhalif is rejected in Zahir al-Riwaya but accepted in later fatwa practice for non-revelatory contexts.

This passage presents a seemingly straightforward fiqh ruling about a muhrim killing a predatory animal, but it quickly opens into a fundamental usul debate: is mafhum mukhalif a valid tool of inference? The Hanafi school has two distinct positions, and understanding which one governs fatwa is essential for correct istidlal. This lesson will guide you through the textual evidence, the internal dispute, and the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Extract the fiqh ruling from the example
Identify the ruling derived from Umar's narration: a muhrim who kills a predator attacking him owes no penalty. This ruling is inferred via mafhum mukhalif from the condition of initiation. Recognize the logical structure: if initiation triggers penalty, then absence of initiation negates penalty.
The derivation is based on a non-Quranic/hadith text (Umar's action and statement).
2
Identify the two positions on mafhum mukhalif
State the Zahir al-Riwaya position: mafhum mukhalif is not a valid method of inference for istidlal. Contrast with the position of Imam Muhammad, al-Khassaf, and others: mafhum mukhalif is valid in legal traditions and everyday speech.
Note that both positions are within the Hanafi school; the dispute is internal.
3
Analyze the scope of each position
The Zahir al-Riwaya restricts the principle to Quran and Sunnah. The opposing view extends it to non-revelatory contexts: fiqh traditions, rational discourse, and common language. This is the key to resolving the apparent contradiction.
Shari'ah texts are treated as having special eloquence that may preclude mafhum.
4
Determine the mufta bihi according to the passage
Allama Birri concludes that the practice (fatwa) is upon the acceptance of mafhum mukhalif as per al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Khassaf, and he knows of no opposition. Thus, for fatwa, the mufta bihi is that mafhum mukhalif is valid in its proper scope.
This is a clear tarjih for fatwa practice despite the Zahir al-Riwaya.

شى عقود رسم المفى
کیا ہے کہ جب درندہ محرم پر حملہ کرے اور وہ اس کو قتل کر دے تو اس پر کوئی جزا واجب نہیں ہے اس روایت کی وجہ سے جو حضرت عمرؓ سے مروی ہے کہ آپ نے ایک درندے کو قتل کیا اور ایک مینڈھے کا دم دیا اور ارشاد فرمایا کہ ہم نے ابتداء کی تھی، اس مسئلے کی شرح کرتے ہوئے اتقانی نے لکھا ہے کہ حضرت عمرؓ نے دم دینے کی وجہ اپنی طرف سے ابتداء کرنے کو بتایا، اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ جب محرم نے قتل کرنے میں ابتداء نہ کی ہو، بلکہ درندے کے حملے کو روکنے کے لیے اس کو قتل کیا ہو تو محرم پر کوئی جزا واجب نہیں ہے، ورنہ حضرت عمر کی بیان کی ہوئی وجہ کا کوئی فائدہ باقی نہ رہے گا۔

وہ بات جو ظہیر یہ میں ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال جائز نہیں ہے، اور یہی ہمارے علماء کی ظاہر روایت ہے، اور وہ بات جس کو امام محمد نے سیر کبیر میں ذکر فرمایا ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال جائز ہے وہ بات ظاہر روایت کے خلاف ہے، کشف کے حواشی میں اس کے مصنف نے لکھا ہے کہ میں نے فوائد ظہیریہ کے باب مــا یـکـره فـی الصلواۃ میں دیکھا ہے کہ مفہوم سے استدلال جائز ہے، اس کو شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے سیر کبیر میں ذکر کیا ہے اور فرمایا ہے کہ امام محمد نے سیر کبیر میں مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال کے جواز پر مسائل کی بنیاد رکھی ہے، امام خصاف کا میلان بھی اسی طرف ہے، اور انھوں نے کتاب الحیل میں مسائل کا اسی پر مدار رکھا ہے، اور مصفی میں ہے کہ کسی چیز کا خصوصیت کے ساتھ تذکرہ کرنا کا اس کے ماسوا کی نفی پر دلالت نہیں کرتا ، ہم کہتے ہیں کہ روایات فقہیہ میں اور لوگوں کی باہمی گفتگو میں اور دلائل عقلیہ میں اس کے ماسوا کی نفی پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ (تعالی کی عبارت پوری ہوئی جو اس کی کتاب النکاح سے منقول ہے ) اور خزانہ الروایات میں ہے کہ فقہی روایت میں مذکور قید اس کے ماسوا سے اس حکم کی نفی کرتا ہے، اور فتاوی سراجیہ میں ہے کہ لوگوں کی ایسی باہمی گفتگو جس کا تعلق اطلاعات اور اخبار وغیرہ سے ہو اس میں کسی چیز کا خصوصیت کے ساتھ ذکر کرنا بالیقین اس کے ماسوا سے اس حکم کی نفی پر دلالت کرتا ہے، سرخسی نے ایسا ہی بیان کیا ہے سراجیہ کی عبارت پوری ہوئی۔ ان عبارات کو نقل کرنے کے بعد علامہ بیری فرماتے ہیں: میں کہتا ہوں کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ اس پر عمل کریں گے جو السیر الکبیر میں ہے، جیسا کہ امام خصاف نے کتاب الحیل میں اس کو اختیار کیا ہے اور میں نے اس قول کی مخالفت کرتے ہوئے کسی کو نہیں دیکھا اور اللہ بہتر جاننے والے ہیں، بیری کی عبارت مکمل ہوئی۔
From the mufti in the chapter... Explanation of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. It is that when a predatory animal attacks a muhrim and he kills it, there is no penalty upon him, due to the narration from Sayyiduna Umar that he killed a predator and gave a sheep as compensation and said: 'We had initiated.' Explaining this issue, Itqani wrote that Sayyiduna Umar attributed the giving of compensation to initiation on his part. From this it is understood that when the muhrim did not initiate in killing, but rather killed to repel the animal's attack, then no penalty is due; otherwise the reason stated by Umar would have no effect. Allama Birri wrote in Sharh al-Ashbah: 'What is in al-Zahiriyyah is that inference from mafhum mukhalif is not permissible, and this is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) of our scholars. And what Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir that inference from mafhum mukhalif is permissible opposes the apparent transmission. In the margins of Kashf, its author wrote: I saw in the chapter on disliked acts in prayer in al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya that inference from mafhum is permissible. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned this in al-Siyar al-Kabir and said that Imam Muhammad based many issues on the permissibility of mafhum mukhalif. Imam al-Khassaf also inclined to this view and based issues in Kitab al-Hiyal on it. In al-Musaffa: mentioning something specifically does not negate what is other than it; we say that in legal traditions (riwayat fiqhiyya), people's conversations, and rational proofs, it does negate the opposite.' The passage from Ta'ali from his book al-Nikah is quoted. In Khizanat al-Riwayat: the condition mentioned in a legal tradition negates the ruling for other than it. In Fatawa Sirajiyyah: in people's conversations pertaining to information and reports, mentioning something specifically certainly negates the ruling for other than it, as Sarakhsi related. The Sirajiyya passage ends. After quoting these passages, Allama Birri says: 'I say that the apparent is to act upon what is in al-Siyar al-Kabir, as Imam al-Khassaf chose it in Kitab al-Hiyal, and I have not seen anyone opposing this view. And Allah knows best.' Birri's statement ends.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage first presents a specific fiqh ruling: a muhrim who kills a predatory animal in self-defense incurs no penalty. This is derived from the incident of Sayyiduna Umar, who gave compensation when he initiated the attack, implying via mafhum mukhalif that without initiation, no compensation is due. The text then transitions to an extended discussion on the validity of mafhum mukhalif as a tool of inference. It cites various authorities: according to the Zahir al-Riwaya (the preferred transmission within the Hanafi school), mafhum mukhalif is not valid for istidlal. However, Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Khassaf accept it, especially in legal traditions and everyday speech. The debate hinges on whether specifying a condition necessarily negates the opposite. The passage ultimately sides with acceptance in non-Qur'anic/hadith contexts, with Birri advocating for acting upon Imam Muhammad's position as no opposition is known.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum mukhalif): The opposite meaning inferred from a conditional or qualified statement; e.g., if a condition is mentioned, the ruling applies only when that condition is present.
ظاہر روایت (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted rulings from the early Hanafi imams, recorded in the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi regarding mafhum mukhalif in the Hanafi school is that it is a valid tool of inference for legal traditions and common speech, though not for direct interpretation of Quran and Sunnah.

Mafhum Mukhalif: Scope and Limitations
Synthesis of rule on mafhum mukhalif in shari'ah vs. non-shari'ah speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of mafhum mukhalif by identifying when it is permissible to use it in istidlal and when it is not, based on Shami's criteria.

Core Idea
Mafhum mukhalif is valid only in non-divine speech and must not contradict an explicit text.

In this passage, Allama Shami distills the earlier discussions into a clear rule for muftis: mafhum mukhalif (inferential meaning from a condition) is accepted in ordinary speech but not in the Qur'an or hadith. He explains why divine speech is different and adds a crucial qualification: the inferred meaning must never contradict an explicit text. This lesson will help you understand exactly when and how to apply this tool in fatwa derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the speech context
Determine whether the text under consideration is from the Lawgiver (Qur'an/Hadith) or from human speech (jurists, common language).
Divine speech is eloquent and may have purposes beyond limiting rulings.
2
If divine speech, analyze the condition's purpose
Check if the condition in the verse or hadith is descriptive of the usual state, rather than a limiting condition. The example of stepdaughters shows that the phrase 'who are in your guardianship' is descriptive.
If descriptive, mafhum mukhalif is not applicable.
3
If human speech, apply mafhum mukhalif per custom
In ordinary speech, specifying a condition customarily implies that the ruling differs when the condition is absent. This is the basis for applying mafhum mukhalif.
This is based on the custom of speakers (urf).
4
Verify no contradiction with an explicit text
Even in human speech, the inferred opposite ruling must not contradict a clear, explicit (sarih) text that states a ruling directly.
If contradiction exists, mafhum mukhalif is rejected.
5
Derive the ruling
Once the above steps are satisfied, you may derive the ruling that the opposite of the mentioned condition holds. Otherwise, the condition is not considered limiting.
This is a tool for istidlal, not a primary source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامہ شامی مذکورہ تمام عبارات کو قتل کرنے کے بعد خلاصہ کے طور پر فرماتے ہیں کہ ان تمام عبارات کا ماحصل یہ ہے کہ شارع کے کلام کے علاوہ میں مفہوم مخالف کو معتبر قرار دیا گیا ہے، شارع کے کلام میں مفہوم کا اعتبار اس لئے نہیں کیا جاتا ہے کیوں کہ شارع کے کلام میں کسی چیز کا صراحتاً تذکرہ ہونے سے یہ بات لازم نہیں آتی ہے کہ اس کا مفاداس کے ماسوا سے حکم کی نفی ہی ہو، اس لیے کہ شارع کا کلام بلاغت کا مخزن ہے، پس شارع کی مراد کبھی کچھ اور بھی ہوتی ہے، جیسے وَرَبَائِبُكُمُ اللَّاتِي فِي حُجُوْرِكُمْ میں فی الحجور کی قید کا فائدہ بالا جماع یہی ہے کہ عام طور پر بیوی کے پہلے شوہر کی بیٹی اس کے دوسرے شوہر کی پرورش میں ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس قید کا ذکر کر دیا گیا، اس کا یہ مطلب بالکل نہیں ہے کہ اگر پہلے شوہر کی بیٹی موجودہ شوہر کی پرورش میں نہ ہو تو اس سے نکاح جائز ہے، اور رہا لوگوں کا کلام تو وہ اس خوبی سے خالی ہوتا ہے، لہذا ان کے کلام میں مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال کیا جائے گا، کیوں کہ لوگوں میں متعارف یہی بات ہے۔
مفہوم مخالف اگر صراحت کے خلاف ہو علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں کہ:

(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٥٦)
ميرا قول: ما لم يخالف لصريح ثبتا
Allama Shami, after quoting all the preceding passages, says as a summary: The gist of all these passages is that mafhum mukhalif has been considered valid in other than the speech of the Lawgiver. In the speech of the Lawgiver, mafhum is not considered, because in His speech, the explicit mention of something does not entail that its meaning is the negation of the ruling for what is other than it, for the Lawgiver's speech is a treasure of eloquence. Thus, His intention may sometimes be something else, like in {your stepdaughters who are in your guardianship}, the benefit of the condition 'who are in your guardianship' is that generally the stepdaughter is under the upbringing of the second husband, so this condition was mentioned. It does not mean that if the stepdaughter is not under the upbringing of the present husband, marriage to her is permissible. As for people's speech, it is devoid of this quality; therefore, in their speech, inference from mafhum mukhalif will be made, because this is what is customary among people. (Then) if the mafhum mukhalif contradicts an explicit text, Allama Shami says: 'My statement: as long as it does not contradict an explicit text' – accepted.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
Allama Shami now synthesizes the earlier debate into a clear rule: mafhum mukhalif is valid in non-Revealed speech (legal traditions, common discourse) but not in the Qur'an or hadith. The reason is that Allah's speech is a treasure of eloquence; specifying a condition may serve a different purpose than negating the opposite. He provides the example of the Qur'anic verse about stepdaughters (Qur'an 4:23): the phrase 'who are in your guardianship' is descriptive of the usual state, not a condition for prohibition. Thus, it does not imply that stepdaughters not in one's care are permissible. In contrast, people's speech typically uses conditions to limit rulings, so mafhum applies. Finally, Shami adds an important qualification taken from the text: mafhum mukhalif is only accepted if it does not conflict with an explicit text (sarih). The page ends mid-statement.

Key Terms
شارع کا کلام (kalam al-shari'): The speech of the Lawgiver, i.e., the Qur'an and hadith.
صراحت (sarih): Explicit or clear text that directly states a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shami's summary, why is mafhum mukhalif not applied to the speech of the Lawgiver (Qur'an and hadith)?
A) Because the Lawgiver's speech is always general and unconditional.
B) Because the Lawgiver's speech is a treasure of eloquence and may have purposes beyond negation of the opposite.
C) Because mafhum mukhalif is fundamentally invalid in all contexts.
D) Because the Sahibayn rejected it.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum mukhalif is a valid tool in non-divine speech only, and must not contradict an explicit text.

Fatwa Application of Mafhum Mukhalif: Shari' vs. People's Speech
Defining the scope of mafhum mukhalif in fatwa practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that mafhum mukhalif is valid only in people's speech and only when not contradicted by an explicit text, and identify when it cannot be used in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fatwa practice, mafhum mukhalif is not valid in the Lawgiver's speech; it is only valid in people's speech and must yield to an explicit text.

This lesson clarifies a critical distinction in Hanafi usul: the validity of mafhum mukhalif depends on whose speech it is. While ordinary people's restrictions logically negate the ruling elsewhere, the Lawgiver's eloquence may have multiple intentions. You will learn when a mufti can rely on mafhum mukhalif and when it must be set aside.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of speech
Determine whether the text in question is from the Lawgiver (Quran, Sunnah) or from people (contracts, statements, oaths). This classification dictates the applicability of mafhum mukhalif.
The passage explicitly distinguishes: Shari' speech vs. people's speech.
2
If Shari' speech, do not use mafhum mukhalif
The Lawgiver's speech is a repository of eloquence; restrictions may be for prevalent circumstances or other purposes, so the opposite implication is not assumed. Example: 'step-daughters in your care' does not imply permission when not in your care.
This is the core Hanafi position.
3
If people's speech, check for explicit contradiction
In people's speech, mafhum mukhalif is generally valid because it follows customary logical implication. However, it is only a proof if it does not contradict an explicit (sarih) text.
Sarih overrides mafhum in all cases.
4
Apply the precedence rule
If a sarih text exists, give it precedence over mafhum mukhalif. If no sarih, mafhum may be used. This is a universal usul principle.
Referenced from al-Tarsusi and usul works on tarjih.
5
Determine the fatwa outcome
State the ruling: for Shari' texts, do not rely on mafhum; for people's texts, rely on mafhum only if no sarih contradicts. Document the reasoning for the fatwa.
The mufta bihi is as stated by al-Shami and al-Birri.

Source Text

میں کہتا ہوں کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ اس پر عمل کریں گے جو السیر الکبیر میں ہے، جیسا کہ امام خصاف نے کتاب الحیل میں اس کو اختیار کیا ہے اور میں نے اس قول کی مخالفت کرتے ہوئے کسی کو نہیں دیکھا اور اللہ بہتر علاوہ میں مفہوم مخالف کو معتبر قرار دیا گیا ہے، شارع کے کلام میں مفہوم کا اعتبار اس لئے نہیں کیا جاتا ہے کیوں کہ شارع کے کلام میں کسی چیز کا صراحتاً تذکرہ ہونے سے یہ بات لازم نہیں آتی ہے کہ اس کا مفہوم اس کے ماسوا سے حکم کی نفی ہی ہو، اس لیے کہ شارع کا کلام بلاغت کا مخزن ہے، پس شارع کی مراد کبھی کچھ اور بھی ہوتی ہے، جیسے وَرَبَائِبُكُمُ اللَّاتِي فِي حُجُوْرِكُمْ میں فی الحجور کی قید کا فائدہ بالا جماع یہی ہے کہ عام طور پر بیوی کے پہلے شوہر کی بیٹی اس کے دوسرے شوہر کی پرورش میں ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس قید کا ذکر کر دیا گیا، اس کا یہ مطلب بالکل نہیں ہے کہ اگر پہلے شوہر کی بیٹی موجودہ شوہر کی پرورش میں نہ ہو تو اس سے نکاح جائز ہے، اور رہا لوگوں کا کلام تو وہ اس خوبی سے خالی ہوتا ہے، لہذا ان کے کلام میں مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال کیا جائے گا، کیوں کہ لوگوں میں متعارف یہی بات ہے۔ مفہوم مخالف اگر صراحت کے خلاف ہو علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں کہ: وو (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٥٦) ميرا قول: ما لم يخالف لصريح ثبتا (جب تک مفہوم مخالف کسی صریح ثابت شدہ بات کے خلاف نہ ہو) کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو ہم نے بیان کیا اس وقت حجت ہے جب کہ وہ کسی صریح بات کے خلاف نہ ہو، کیوں کہ صریح بات مفہوم پر مقدم ہوتی ہے، جیسا کہ طرسوی وغیرہ نے اس کی صراحت کی ہے، اور ائمہ اصول نے اس کو ترجیح اولہ کی بحث میں ذکر کیا ہے، کیوں کہ جو حضرات دلائلِ شرعیہ میں مفہوم مخالف کے معتبر ہونے کے قائل ہیں وہ اسی صورت میں اس کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں جب کہ کوئی صریح بات اس کے خلاف موجود نہ ہو، ورنہ صریح کو مقدم کیا جائے گا اور مفہوم کو لغو قرار دیا جائے گا۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٥٧)
The mufti in [??] of the explanation of Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 'by certainty, it indicates the negation of this ruling from other than it.' Al-Sarakhsi has stated similarly. The text of Sirajiyya is completed. After quoting these expressions, Allama al-Birri says: I say: apparently we should act upon what is in al-Siyar al-Kabir, just as Imam al-Khassaf has chosen it in Kitab al-Hiyal, and I have not seen anyone opposing this statement. And Allah knows best. The words of al-Birri are complete. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 154) Allama al-Shami, after quoting all the above expressions, says as a summary: The gist of all these expressions is that mafhum mukhalif (opposite implication) is considered valid in other than the speech of the Lawgiver. In the speech of the Lawgiver, maqhum is not considered because the mere explicit mention of something in the Lawgiver's speech does not necessitate that its implication is the negation of the ruling from other than it. This is because the Lawgiver's speech is the repository of eloquence; thus, the intent of the Lawgiver may sometimes be something else. For example, in (Quran 4:23) 'and your step-daughters who are in your care' the restriction 'who are in your care' is beneficial for the prevalent situation: usually the daughter of the wife from the previous husband is under the care of the second husband. Therefore this restriction was mentioned. It does not mean at all that if the step-daughter is not under the care of the current husband, then marriage to her is permissible. As for the speech of people, it is devoid of this quality; therefore, in their speech, one can use mafhum mukhalif as evidence, because this is the custom among people. As for when mafhum mukhalif contradicts an explicit text, Allama al-Shami says: [waw] (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 156) My statement: 'as long as it does not contradict an explicit established [text]' means that mafhum mukhalif, according to the detail we have mentioned, is a proof only when it does not contradict any explicit text, because the explicit text takes precedence over the implication. This has been clarified by Tarsusi and others, and the scholars of usul have mentioned it in the discussion of tarjih bi al-awla. Because those who consider mafhum mukhalif valid among the Shari' proofs only accept it when there is no explicit text opposed to it; otherwise, the explicit is given precedence and the implication is considered null. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 157)
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage addresses the Hanafi ruling regarding the validity of mafhum mukhalif (opposite implication) in the context of issuing fatwas. The passage begins by citing earlier authorities that mafhum mukhalif is considered valid in the speech of people but not in the speech of the Lawgiver (Shari'). The reason given is that the Lawgiver's speech is highly eloquent and may have multiple purposes; a restriction mentioned may be for the prevalent situation rather than to negate the ruling for other cases. The example of the Quranic verse about step-daughters (4:23) is provided: the phrase 'who are in your care' does not imply that if they are not in your care, marriage is permissible. In contrast, people's speech follows logical implication, so their restrictions indicate negation of the ruling elsewhere. The passage then clarifies a further condition: mafhum mukhalif is valid only as long as it does not contradict an explicit (sarih) text. If there is a clear explicit text on the matter, the explicit takes precedence over the implication. This is a common principle in usul al-fiqh known as tarjih al-naas 'ala al-mafhum. The passage quotes al-Tarsusi and others to confirm this. Thus, the mufti must be careful: he can use mafhum mukhalif from people's speech, but for Shari' texts, he should apply the explicit meaning unless there is no explicit, and then mafhum may be considered only if it does not oppose an explicit.

Key Terms
مَفْهُوم مُخَالِف (mafhum mukhalif): The implied opposite meaning derived from a restricted or qualified statement, e.g., if a condition is mentioned, the ruling is negated when the condition is absent.
صَرِيح (sarih): An explicit text or statement that clearly establishes a ruling without need for implication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is mafhum mukhalif considered a valid proof in Hanafi fiqh?
A) In both the speech of the Lawgiver and people's speech, without exception.
B) Only in people's speech, and only when it does not contradict an explicit text.
C) Only in the speech of the Lawgiver, and only when it has a clear restriction.
D) In neither, as all implications are invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa practice, mafhum mukhalif is valid only in people's speech and only if not contradicted by an explicit text; it is not valid in the speech of the Lawgiver.

Explicit Text Overrides Mafhum Mukhālif in Fatwa
Explaining the rule that explicit text overrides mafhum mukhālif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that explicit text (ṣarīḥ) takes precedence over mafhum mukhālif when deriving fatwas, and identify when mafhum mukhālif is considered valid.

Core Idea
Explicit text always overrides implied opposite meaning; mafhum mukhālif is conditional.

In issuing fatwas, a mufti often encounters textual evidence that may have both an explicit meaning and an implied opposite meaning. Hanafi usul, as well as other schools that accept mafhum mukhālif, establish a clear hierarchy: if an explicit text conflicts with a mafhum, the explicit prevails. This lesson clarifies that rule and its application in fatwa practice, ensuring that rulings are grounded in direct textual statements rather than inferred meanings that might contradict them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting evidences
Given a scenario, locate the explicit textual statement (ṣarīḥ/manṭūq) and the potentially conflicting mafhum mukhālif derived from another text. Clearly state both.
2
Apply the hierarchy rule
Recall the rule from this passage: explicit text takes precedence over mafhum mukhālif. In case of conflict, the explicit is used and the mafhum is discarded.
3
Conclude which evidence is operative
State the final ruling based on the explicit text. Explain why the mafhum is not considered, referencing the principle of tarjīḥ.
This step ensures the fatwa is built on the strongest textual basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثابت شدہ بات کے خلاف نہ ہو) کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو ہم نے بیان کیا اس وقت حجت ہے جب کہ وہ کسی صریح بات کے خلاف نہ ہو، کیوں کہ صریح بات مفہوم پر مقدم ہوتی ہے، جیسا کہ طرسوی وغیرہ نے اس کی صراحت کی ہے، اور ائمہ اصول نے اس کو ترجیح اولہ کی بحث میں ذکر کیا ہے، کیوں کہ جو حضرات دلائلِ شرعیہ میں مفہوم مخالف کے معتبر ہونے کے قائل ہیں وہ اسی صورت میں اس کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں جب کہ کوئی صریح بات اس کے خلاف موجود نہ ہو، ورنہ صریح کو مقدم کیا جائے گا اور مفہوم کو لغو قرار دیا جائے گا۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٥٧)
The meaning of 'should not contradict an established matter' is that the mafhum mukhālif is authoritative according to the detail we have mentioned only when it does not contradict an explicit text, because the explicit text takes precedence over the implicit meaning. As al-Tarasūsī and others have clarified, and the imams of usul have mentioned this in the discussion of preference (tarjīh) because those who consider mafhum mukhālif as valid among the shar'i evidences only consider it valid when there is no explicit text contradicting it; otherwise, the explicit is given precedence and the implicit is considered invalid.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule from the commentary on 'Uqūd Rasm al-Muftī. It clarifies the hierarchy between explicit text (manṭūq) and implicit meaning (mafhūm mukhālif). The author explains that mafhum mukhālif is only authoritative when it does not contradict a clear, explicit textual statement. If there is a conflict, the explicit text is given precedence, and the mafhum is discarded. This is a fundamental principle of uṣūl al-fiqh agreed upon by those who accept mafhum mukhālif as a valid evidence. The rule ensures that fatwas are based on direct textual evidence rather than inferred meanings that might contradict the plain wording.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (mafhūm mukhālif): The implied opposite meaning (a contrario sense) derived from a text.
صریح (ṣarīḥ): Explicit, clear textual statement (manṭūq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, mafhum mukhālif is valid only when:
A) It is supported by consensus
B) It does not contradict an explicit text
C) It is from a stronger narrator
D) It relates to worship

Key Takeaway
When issuing a fatwa, always check for explicit texts that may contradict a derived mafhum mukhālif; the explicit text takes precedence.
